Anthony_Wagner	Sir Anthony Richard Wagner , KCB , KCVO , FSA ( 6 September 1908 - 5 May 1995 ) was a long-serving officer of arms at the College of Arms in London .
Anthony_Wagner	He served as Garter Principal King of Arms before retiring to the post of Clarenceux King of Arms .
Anthony_Wagner	He was one of the most prolific authors on subjects of the heraldry and genealogy of the 20th century .
Anthony_Wagner	Wagner was born to a family of German Silesian origin ( see Burke 's `` Landed Gentry '' ) .
Anthony_Wagner	His ancestor , Melchior Wagner , arrived in England from the Saxon city of Coburg in 1709 and became hatter to George I of Great Britain .
Anthony_Wagner	At an early age Wagner developed a taste for genealogy , and invented an imaginary realm which he could people to taste .
Anthony_Wagner	His father ran a day-school in London .
Anthony_Wagner	Scholarships took Wagner to Eton College and then to Balliol College at Oxford .
Anthony_Wagner	Eventually he entered the College of Arms as Portcullis Pursuivant of Arms in Ordinary in 1931 .
Anthony_Wagner	Wagner did not marry until he was 44 , but in 1953 made a happy alliance with Gillian , daughter of Major H.A.R. Graham .
Anthony_Wagner	In addition to taking over his father 's house in Chelsea Square they acquired a country cottage at Aldeburgh , Suffolk .
Anthony_Wagner	He was survived by two sons , one of whom is a distinguished artist , and a daughter .
Anthony_Wagner	After Sir Anthony 's death in 1995 , he was buried at Aldeburgh following a funeral service at the Church of St Benet Paul 's Wharf , which has been the religious home of the College of Arms since 1555 .
Anthony_Wagner	Wagner joined the College of Arms as Portcullis Pursuivant of Arms in Ordinary in 1931 .
Anthony_Wagner	He was promoted to Richmond Herald of Arms in Ordinary in 1943 and Garter Principal King of Arms in 1961 .
Anthony_Wagner	In 1978 he retired to the subordinate position of Clarenceux King of Arms .
Anthony_Wagner	He was a firm believer in the view that appointments to the college were for life .
Anthony_Wagner	As a herald he enjoyed a very large practice and was able to train up a number of skilled and well-qualified assistants who later became officers of arms .
Anthony_Wagner	His professional library was enormous , but he was also able to build up an important collection of early heraldic manuscripts from the Clumber and other sales .
Anthony_Wagner	During World War II he served in the War Office for four years , and then moved to the Ministry of Town and Country Planning , where he rose to be Principal Private Secretary to a series of ministers .
Anthony_Wagner	Although he contemplated remaining in the Ministry , he returned to the College of Arms in 1946 and took over the extensive practice of Alfred Butler , Windsor Herald .
Anthony_Wagner	One idea , which he pursued persistently , was the establishment of a museum in which to display the treasures of the College of Arms itself .
Anthony_Wagner	Initially it was hoped to erect a building adjacent to the college , and a most interesting design was commissioned from Raymond Erith ; this became impossible because of the increasing financial demands of repairs to the college itself .
Anthony_Wagner	For it has to be remembered that the Heralds , as a body corporate , receive no subvention from any national source ; their own stipends were fixed in the 17th century and have not been raised since .
Anthony_Wagner	But in 1981 the Heralds ' Museum was at last opened in part of the Tower of London .
Anthony_Wagner	To those who wish to gain some idea of the resources of the college , Wagner 's own Records and Collections of the College of Arms ( 1952 ) is an invaluable short guide .
Anthony_Wagner	Wagner continued to visit the College of Arms and attend meetings of its chapter .
Anthony_Wagner	With his departure the world of heraldry and genealogy lost a scholar of majestic stature , though his numerous works keep his memory alive .
Anthony_Wagner	Wagner had many interests outside the world and work of the College of Arms .
Anthony_Wagner	He belonged to the Vintners ' Company , serving as Master from 1973 to 1974 , and was a member of a number of important dining clubs including the Society of Dilettanti , the antiquarian Cocked Hats , and the bibliophilic Roxburghe Club .
Anthony_Wagner	A number of large projects engaged his attention and enthusiasm .
Anthony_Wagner	One , which arose from the Harleian Society , was an endeavor to list and describe the surviving English Rolls of Arms : to this series ( CEMRA ) Wagner contributed the first volume .
Anthony_Wagner	Another project , connected with the Society of Antiquaries of London , was a revised edition of the Ordinary of Arms originally produced by Papworth .
Anthony_Wagner	The first volume appeared in 1992 .
Anthony_Wagner	It is fair to say that through his life genealogy occupied the foremost place in Wagner 's affections , but his earliest publications made highly important contributions to the study of heraldry .
Anthony_Wagner	Issues of State Ceremonial took third priority .
Anthony_Wagner	His Historic Heraldry of England ( 1939 ) derived initially from an exhibition of panels in America , but drew a stern and scholarly line between those great men who were truly armigerous and those who were not .
Anthony_Wagner	On the other hand , his Heralds and Heraldry in the Middle Ages ( also 1939 ) shed new light on the development of the functions of the earliest officers of arms .
Anthony_Wagner	Many years later he traced the whole story of the College of Arms in a massive volume entitled Heralds of England ( 1967 ) .
Anthony_Wagner	Of all Wagner 's genealogical writings , his English Genealogy ( 1960 , and since revised ) is standard reference in any well-stocked public library and on many private shelves .
Anthony_Wagner	Many of his conclusions were rehearsed and reinforced in Pedigree and Progress ( 1975 ) , where an important group of essays is annotated and brought up to date .
Anthony_Wagner	Always he stressed the mobility of social life and class in the course of English history , and in maintaining this view ran contrary to the opinions of some professional English historians .
Anthony_Wagner	His office had been highly mechanised from an early stage , but all the more so once he became blind in 1984 , whereupon , making every use of the aids of modern science , he bore his affliction with patience and dexterity .
Anthony_Wagner	His autobiography , A Herald 's Way ( 1988 ) he dictated .
Anthony_Wagner	He was also a staunch supporter of hereditary peers and defended their presence in the House of Lords in an article in the Times on 30 January 1969 which became the foreword to the 1970 edition of Burke 's Peerage .
AAC	Advanced Audio Coding ( AAC ) is a standardized , lossy compression and encoding scheme for digital audio .
AAC	Designed to be the successor of the MP3 format , AAC generally achieves better sound quality than MP3 at similar bit rates .
AAC	AAC has been standardized by ISO and IEC , as part of the MPEG-2 and MPEG-4 specifications .
AAC	Part of the AAC known as High-Efficiency Advanced Audio Coding ( HE-AAC ) which is part of MPEG-4 Audio is also adopted into digital radio standards like DAB + and Digital Radio Mondiale , as well as mobile television standards DVB-H and ATSC-M\/H .
AAC	AAC supports inclusion of 48 full-bandwidth ( up to 96 kHz ) audio channels in one stream plus 16 low frequency effects ( LFE , limited to 120 Hz ) channels , up to 16 `` coupling '' or dialog channels , and up to 16 data streams .
AAC	The quality for stereo is satisfactory to modest requirements at 96 kbit\/s in joint stereo mode ; however , hi-fi transparency demands data rates of at least 128 kbit\/s ( VBR ) .
AAC	The MPEG-2 audio tests showed that AAC meets the requirements referred to as `` transparent '' for the ITU at 128 kbit\/s for stereo , and 320 kbit\/s for 5.1 audio .
AAC	AAC is also the default or standard audio format for YouTube , iPhone , iPod , iPad , Nintendo DSi , iTunes , DivX Plus Web Player and PlayStation 3 .
AAC	It is supported on PlayStation Portable , Wii ( with the Photo Channel 1.1 update installed ) , Sony Walkman MP3 series and later , Sony Ericsson ; Nokia , Android , BlackBerry , and webOS-based mobile phones , with the use of a converter .
AAC	AAC has also seen some adoption on in-dash car audio especially on high-end units such as the Pioneer AVIC series .
AAC	AAC was developed with the cooperation and contributions of companies including AT&T Bell Laboratories , Fraunhofer IIS , Dolby Laboratories , Sony Corporation and Nokia .
AAC	It was officially declared an international standard by the Moving Picture Experts Group in April 1997 .
AAC	It is specified both as Part 7 of the MPEG-2 standard , and Subpart 4 in Part 3 of the MPEG-4 standard .
AAC	In 1997 , AAC was first introduced as MPEG-2 Part 7 , formally known as ISO\/IEC 13818-7 :1997 .
AAC	This part of MPEG-2 was a new part , since MPEG-2 already included MPEG-2 Part 3 , formally known as ISO\/IEC 13818-3 : MPEG-2 BC ( Backwards Compatible ) .
AAC	Therefore , MPEG-2 Part 7 is also known as MPEG-2 NBC ( Non-Backward Compatible ) , because it is not compatible with the MPEG-1 audio formats ( MP1 , MP2 and MP3 ) .
AAC	MPEG-2 Part 7 defined three profiles : Low-Complexity profile ( AAC-LC \/ LC-AAC ) , Main profile ( AAC Main ) and Scalable Sampling Rate profile ( AAC-SSR ) .
AAC	AAC-LC profile consists of a base format very much like AT&T 's Perceptual Audio Coding ( PAC ) coding format , with the addition of temporal noise shaping ( TNS ) , the Dolby Kaiser Window ( described below ) , a nonuniform quantizer , and a reworking of the bitstream format to handle up to 16 stereo channels , 16 mono channels , 16 low-frequency effect ( LFE ) channels and 16 commentary channels in one bitstream .
AAC	The Main profile adds a set of recursive predictors that are calculated on each tap of the filterbank .
AAC	The SSR uses a 4-band PQMF filterbank , with four shorter filterbanks following , in order to allow for scalable sampling rates .
AAC	In 1999 , MPEG-2 Part 7 was updated and included in the MPEG-4 family of standard and became known as MPEG-4 Part 3 , MPEG-4 Audio or ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :1999 .
AAC	This update included several improvements .
AAC	One of these improvements was the addition of Audio Object Types which are used to allow interoperability with a diverse range of other audio formats such as TwinVQ , CELP , HVXC , Text-To-Speech Interface and MPEG-4 Structured Audio .
AAC	Another notable addition in this version of the AAC standard is Perceptual Noise Substitution ( PNS ) .
AAC	In that regard , the AAC profiles ( AAC-LC , AAC Main and AAC-SSR profiles ) are combined with perceptual noise substitution and are defined in the MPEG-4 audio standard as Audio Object Types .
AAC	MPEG-4 Audio Object Types are combined in four MPEG-4 Audio profiles : Main ( which includes most of the MPEG-4 Audio Object Types ) , Scalable ( AAC LC , AAC LTP , CELP , HVXC , TwinVQ , Wavetable Synthesis , TTSI ) , Speech ( CELP , HVXC , TTSI ) and Low Rate Synthesis ( Wavetable Synthesis , TTSI ) .
AAC	The reference software for MPEG-4 Part 3 is specified in MPEG-4 Part 5 and the conformance bit-streams are specified in MPEG-4 Part 4 .
AAC	MPEG-4 Audio remains backward-compatible with MPEG-2 Part 7 .
AAC	The MPEG-4 Audio Version 2 ( ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :1999 \/ Amd 1:2000 ) defined new audio object types : the low delay AAC ( AAC-LD ) object type , bit-sliced arithmetic coding ( BSAC ) object type , parametric audio coding using harmonic and individual line plus noise and error resilient ( ER ) versions of object types .
AAC	It also defined four new audio profiles : High Quality Audio Profile , Low Delay Audio Profile , Natural Audio Profile and Mobile Audio Internetworking Profile .
AAC	The HE-AAC Profile ( AAC LC with SBR ) and AAC Profile ( AAC LC ) were first standardized in ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :2001 \/ Amd 1:2003 .
AAC	The HE-AAC v2 Profile ( AAC LC with SBR and Parametric Stereo ) was first specified in ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :2005 \/ Amd 2:2006 .
AAC	The Parametric Stereo audio object type used in HE-AAC v2 was first defined in ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :2001 \/ Amd 2:2004 .
AAC	The current version of the AAC standard is defined in ISO\/IEC 14496-3 :2009 .
AAC	AAC + v2 is also standardized by ETSI ( European Telecommunications Standards Institute ) as TS 102005 .
AAC	The MPEG-4 Part 3 standard also contains other ways of compressing sound .
AAC	These include lossless compression formats , synthetic audio and low bit-rate compression formats generally used for speech .
AAC	Advanced Audio Coding is designed to be the successor of the MPEG-1 Audio Layer 3 , known as MP3 format , which was specified by ISO\/IEC in 11172-3 ( MPEG-1 Audio ) and 13818-3 ( MPEG-2 Audio ) .
AAC	Blind tests show that AAC demonstrates greater sound quality and transparency than MP3 for files coded at the same bit rate .
AAC	Improvements include : More sample frequencies ( from 8 to 96 kHz ) than MP3 ( 16 to 48 kHz ) Up to 48 channels ( MP3 supports up to two channels in MPEG-1 mode and up to 5.1 channels in MPEG-2 mode ) Arbitrary bit-rates and variable frame length .
AAC	Standardized constant bit rate with bit reservoir .
AAC	Higher efficiency and simpler filterbank ( rather than MP3 's hybrid coding , AAC uses a pure MDCT ) Higher coding efficiency for stationary signals ( AAC uses a blocksize of 1024 or 960 samples , allowing more efficient coding than MP3 's 576 sample blocks ) Higher coding accuracy for transient signals ( AAC uses a blocksize of 128 or 120 samples , allowing more accurate coding than MP3 's 192 sample blocks ) Can use Kaiser-Bessel derived window function to eliminate spectral leakage at the expense of widening the main lobe .
AAC	Much better handling of audio frequencies above 16 kHz .
AAC	More flexible joint stereo ( different methods can be used in different frequency ranges ) Adds additional modules ( tools ) to increase compression efficiency : TNS , Backwards Prediction , PNS etc. .
AAC	.
AAC	These modules can be combined to constitute different encoding profiles .
AAC	Overall , the AAC format allows developers more flexibility to design codecs than MP3 does , and corrects many of the design choices made in the original MPEG-1 audio specification .
AAC	This increased flexibility often leads to more concurrent encoding strategies and , as a result , to more efficient compression .
AAC	However , in terms of whether AAC is better than MP3 , the advantages of AAC are not entirely decisive , and the MP3 specification , although antiquated , has proven surprisingly robust in spite of considerable flaws .
AAC	AAC and HE-AAC are better than MP3 at low bit rates ( typically less than 128 kilobits per second ) .
AAC	This is especially true at very low bit rates where the superior stereo coding , pure MDCT , and better transform window sizes leave MP3 unable to compete .
AAC	While the MP3 format has near-universal hardware and software support , primarily due to MP3 being the format of choice during the crucial first few years of widespread music file-sharing\/distribution over the internet , AAC is a strong contender due to some unwavering industry support .
AAC	AAC takes a modular approach to encoding .
AAC	Depending on the complexity of the bitstream to be encoded , the desired performance and the acceptable output , implementers may create profiles to define which of a specific set of tools they want to use for a particular application .
AAC	The MPEG-2 Part 7 standard ( Advanced Audio Coding ) was first published in 1997 and offers three default profiles : Low Complexity ( LC ) - the simplest and most widely used and supported ; Main Profile ( Main ) - like the LC profile , with the addition of backwards prediction ; Scalable Sample Rate ( SSR ) ( MPEG-4 AAC-SSR ) - a.k.a. Sample-Rate Scalable ( SRS ) ; The MPEG-4 Part 3 standard ( MPEG-4 Audio ) defined various new compression tools ( a.k.a. Audio Object Types ) and their usage in brand new profiles .
AAC	AAC is not used in some of the MPEG-4 Audio profiles .
AAC	The MPEG-2 Part 7 AAC LC profile , AAC Main profile and AAC SSR profile are combined with Perceptual Noise Substitution and defined in the MPEG-4 Audio standard as Audio Object Types ( under the name AAC LC , AAC Main and AAC SSR ) .
AAC	These are combined with other Object Types in MPEG-4 Audio profiles .
AAC	Here is a list of some audio profiles defined in the MPEG-4 standard : Main Audio Profile - defined in 1999 , uses most of the MPEG-4 Audio Object Types ( AAC Main , AAC-LC , AAC-SSR , AAC-LTP , AAC Scalable , TwinVQ , CELP , HVXC , TTSI , Main synthesis ) Scalable Audio Profile - defined in 1999 , uses AAC-LC , AAC-LTP , AAC Scalable , TwinVQ , CELP , HVXC , TTSI .
AAC	Speech Audio Profile - defined in 1999 , uses CELP , HVXC , TTSI .
AAC	Synthetic Audio Profile - defined in 1999 , TTSI , Main synthesis .
AAC	High Quality Audio Profile - defined in 2000 , uses AAC-LC , AAC-LTP , AAC Scalable , CELP , ER-AAC-LC , ER-AAC-LTP , ER-AAC Scalable , ER-CELP .
AAC	Low Delay Audio Profile - defined in 2000 , uses CELP , HVXC , TTSI , ER-AAC-LD , ER-CELP , ER-HVXC .
AAC	Mobile Audio Internetworking Profile - defined in 2000 , uses ER-AAC-LC , ER-AAC-Scalable , ER-TwinVQ , ER-BSAC , ER-AAC-LD .
AAC	AAC Profile - defined in 2003 , uses AAC-LC .
AAC	High Efficiency AAC Profile - defined in 2003 , uses AAC-LC , SBR .
AAC	High Efficiency AAC v2 Profile - defined in 2006 , uses AAC-LC , SBR , PS .
AAC	( One of many improvements in MPEG-4 Audio is the Object Type - Long Term Prediction ( LTP ) , which is an improvement of the Main profile using a forward predictor with lower computational complexity . )
AAC	Depending on the AAC profile and the MP3 encoder , 96 kbit\/s AAC can give nearly the same or better perceptual quality as 128 kbit\/s MP3 .
AAC	Applying error protection enables error correction up to a certain extent .
AAC	Error correcting codes are usually applied equally to the whole payload .
AAC	However , since different parts of an AAC payload show different sensitivity to transmission errors , this would not be a very efficient approach .
AAC	The AAC payload can be subdivided into parts with different error sensitivities .
AAC	Independent error correcting codes can be applied to any of these parts using the Error Protection ( EP ) tool defined in MPEG-4 Audio standard .
AAC	This toolkit provides the error correcting capability to the most sensitive parts of the payload in order to keep the additional overhead low .
AAC	The toolkit is backwardly compatible with simpler and pre-existing AAC decoders .
AAC	A great deal of the tool kit 's error correction functions are based around spreading information about the audio signal more evenly in the datastream .
AAC	Error Resilience ( ER ) techniques can be used to make the coding scheme itself more robust against errors .
AAC	For AAC , three custom-tailored methods were developed and defined in MPEG-4 Audio .
AAC	Huffman Codeword Reordering ( HCR ) to avoid error propagation within spectral data ; Virtual Codebooks ( VCB11 ) to detect serious errors within spectral data ; Reversible Variable Length Code ( RVLC ) to reduce error propagation within scale factor data .
AAC	The MPEG-4 Low Delay Audio Coder ( AAC-LD ) is designed to combine the advantages of perceptual audio coding with the low delay necessary for two-way communication .
AAC	It is closely derived from the MPEG-2 Advanced Audio Coding ( AAC ) format .
AAC	In December 2003 , Japan started broadcasting terrestrial DTV ISDB-T standard that implements MPEG-2 video and MPEG-2 AAC audio .
AAC	In April 2006 Japan started broadcasting the ISDB-T mobile sub-program , called 1seg , that was the first implementation of video H. 264\/AVC with audio HE-AAC in Terrestrial HDTV broadcasting service on the planet .
AAC	In December 2007 , Brazil started broadcasting terrestrial DTV standard called International ISDB-Tb that implements video coding H. 264\/AVC with audio AAC-LC on main program ( single or multi ) and video H. 264\/AVC with audio HE-AACv2 in the 1seg mobile sub-program .
AAC	The ETSI , the standards governing body for the DVB suite , supports AAC , HE-AAC and HE-AAC v2 audio coding in DVB applications since at least 2004 .
AAC	DVB broadcasts which use the H. 264 compression for video normally use HE-AAC for audio .
AAC	In April 2003 , Apple brought mainstream attention to AAC by announcing that its iTunes and iPod products would support songs in MPEG-4 AAC format ( via a firmware update for older iPods ) .
AAC	Customers could download music in a closed-source Digital Rights Management ( DRM ) - restricted form of AAC ( see FairPlay ) via the iTunes Store or create files without DRM from their own CDs using iTunes .
AAC	In later years , Apple began offering music videos and movies , which also use AAC for audio encoding .
AAC	On May 29 , 2007 , Apple began selling songs and music videos free of DRM from participating record labels .
AAC	These files mostly adhere to the AAC standard and are playable on many non-Apple products but they do include custom iTunes information such as album artwork and a purchase receipt , so as to identify the customer in case the file is leaked out onto peer-to-peer networks .
AAC	It is possible , however , to remove these custom tags to restore interoperability with players that conform strictly to the AAC specification .
AAC	As of January 6 , 2009 , nearly all music on the iTunes Store became DRM-free , with the remainder becoming DRM-free by the end of March 2009 .
AAC	iTunes supports a `` Variable bit rate '' ( VBR ) encoding option which encodes AAC tracks in an `` Average bit rate '' ( ABR ) scheme .
AAC	As of September 2009 , Apple has added support for HE-AAC ( which is fully part of the MP4 standard ) only for radio streams , not file playback , and iTunes still lacks support for true VBR encoding .
AAC	The underlying QuickTime API does offer a true VBR encoding profile however .
AAC	For a number of years , many mobile phones from manufacturers such as Nokia , Motorola , Samsung , Sony Ericsson , BenQ-Siemens and Philips have supported AAC playback .
AAC	The first such phone was the Nokia 5510 released in 2002 which also plays MP3s .
AAC	However , this phone was a commercial failure and such phones with integrated music players did not gain mainstream popularity until 2005 when the trend of having AAC as well as MP3 support continued .
AAC	Most new smartphones and music-themed phones support playback of these formats .
AAC	Sony Ericsson phones support various AAC formats in MP4 container .
AAC	AAC-LC is supported in all phones beginning with K700 , phones beginning with W550 have support of HE-AAC .
AAC	The latest devices such as the P990 , K610 , W890i and later support HE-AAC v2 .
AAC	Nokia XpressMusic and other new generation Nokia multimedia phones like N - and E-Series : also support AAC format in LC , HE , M4A and HEv2 profiles .
AAC	BlackBerry : RIM 's latest series of Smartphones such as the 8100 ( `` Pearl '' ) , 9500 ( `` Storm '' ) and 8800 support AAC .
AAC	Apple 's iPhone supports AAC and FairPlay protected AAC files formerly used as the default encoding format in the iTunes store until the removal of DRM restrictions in March 2009 .
AAC	All recent Android phones support AAC-LC , HE-AAC and HE-AAC v2 in MP4 or M4A containers along with several other audio formats .
AAC	From Android 3.1 also raw ADTS files are supported .
AAC	Android 4.0 can also encode these kind of files .
AAC	The HTC Dream ( Also known as the T-Mobile G1 ) is described as supporting certain subset of the full AAC format .
AAC	As of 2009-04-13 at least several forms of AAC files played while others did not play .
AAC	WebOS by HP\/Palm supports AAC , AAC + , eAAC + , and .
AAC	m4a containers in its native music player as well as several third-party players .
AAC	However , it does not support Apple 's FairPlay DRM files downloaded from iTunes .
AAC	Windows Phone 7 : WP7 's Silverlight runtime supports AAC-LC , HE-AAC and HE-AAC v2 decoding .
AAC	A very common program supporting AAC playback is Flash Player , version 9 , update 3 and above .
AAC	Since Flash Player is also a browser plugin , it can play AAC files through a browser as well .
AAC	The Rockbox open source firmware ( available for multiple portable players ) also offers support for AAC to varying degrees , depending on the model of player and the AAC profile .
AAC	Optional iPod support ( playback of unprotected AAC files ) for the Xbox 360 is available as a free download from Xbox Live .
AAC	Almost all current computer media players include built-in decoders for AAC , or can utilize a library to decode it .
AAC	On Microsoft Windows , DirectShow can be used this way with the corresponding filters to enable AAC playback in any DirectShow based player .
AAC	Mac OS X supports AAC via the QuickTime libraries .
AAC	Software player applications of particular note include : 3ivx MPEG-4 - A suite of DirectShow and QuickTime plugins which support AAC encoding and\/or AAC \/ HE-AAC decoding in any DirectShow application .
AAC	CorePlayer also supports LC and HE AAC .
AAC	Easy CD-DA Extractor for Windows , CD Ripper and audio converter , which includes an AAC encoder that supports LC and HE AAC .
AAC	ffdshow is a free open source DirectShow filter for Microsoft Windows operating systems that uses FAAD2 to support AAC decoding .
AAC	foobar2000 is a freeware audio player for Windows that supports LC and HE AAC .
AAC	JAAD is an open-source decoder written in Java .
AAC	K-Multimedia Player also supports AAC .
AAC	KSP Sound Player also supports AAC .
AAC	MediaMonkey .
AAC	Media Player Classic Home Cinema .
AAC	MPlayer or xine are often used as AAC decoders on Linux or Macintosh .
AAC	RealPlayer includes RealNetworks ' RealAudio 10 AAC encoder .
AAC	Songbird for Windows , Linux and Mac OS X supports AAC , including the DRM rights management encoding used for purchased music from the iTunes Store , with a plug-in .
AAC	Sony SonicStage also support AAC .
AAC	VLC media player supports playback and encoding of MP4 and AAC files .
AAC	Winamp for Windows , which includes an AAC encoder that supports LC and HE AAC ; Windows Media Player 12 , released with Windows 7 , supports playback of AAC files natively .
AAC	Another Real product , Rhapsody supports the RealAudio AAC codec , in addition to offering subscription tracks encoded with AAC .
AAC	XBMC ( XBox Media Center ) supports both AAC ( LC and HE ) on modified Xbox game-consoles .
AAC	XMMS supports mp4 playback using a plugin provided by the faad2 library .
AAC	Some of these players ( e.g. , foobar2000 , Winamp , and VLC ) also support the decoding of ADTS ( Audio Data Transport Stream ) or MP4-contained AAC streamed over HTTP using the SHOUTcast protocol .
AAC	Plug-ins for Winamp and foobar2000 enable the creation of such streams .
AAC	In May 2006 , Nero AG released an AAC encoding tool free of charge , Nero Digital Audio ( Nero AAC Codec ) , which is capable of encoding LC-AAC , HE-AAC and HE-AAC v2 streams .
AAC	The tool is a Command Line Interface tool only .
AAC	A separate utility is also included to decode to PCM WAV .
AAC	Various tools including the foobar2000 audio player , MediaCoder , MeGUI encoding front end and dBpoweramp can provide a GUI for this encoder .
AAC	FAAC and FAAD2 stand for Freeware Advanced Audio Coder and Decoder 2 respectively .
AAC	FAAC supports audio object types LC , Main and LTP .
AAC	FAAD2 supports audio object types LC , Main , LTP , SBR and PS .
AAC	Although FAAD2 is free software , FAAC is not free software .
AAC	FFmpeg 's libavcodec library contains free software codecs for both encoding and decoding AAC ( encoding is experimental ) .
Absolute_zero	Absolute zero is the theoretical temperature at which entropy reaches its minimum value .
Absolute_zero	The laws of thermodynamics state that absolute zero can not be reached using only thermodynamic means .
Absolute_zero	A system at absolute zero still possesses quantum mechanical zero-point energy , the energy of its ground state .
Absolute_zero	The kinetic energy of the ground state can not be removed .
Absolute_zero	However , in the classical interpretation it is zero and the thermal energy of matter vanishes .
Absolute_zero	The zero point of any thermodynamic temperature scale , such as Kelvin or Rankine , is set at absolute zero .
Absolute_zero	By international agreement , absolute zero is defined as 0K on the Kelvin scale and as − 273.15 ° on the Celsius scale .
Absolute_zero	This equates to − 459.67 ° on the Fahrenheit scale and 0 R on the Rankine scale .
Absolute_zero	Scientists have achieved temperatures very close to absolute zero , where matter exhibits quantum effects such as superconductivity and superfluidity .
Absolute_zero	One of the first to discuss the possibility of an absolute minimal temperature was Robert Boyle .
Absolute_zero	His 1665 New Experiments and Observations touching Cold , articulated the dispute known as the primum frigidum .
Absolute_zero	The concept was well known among naturalists of the time .
Absolute_zero	Some contended an absolute minimum temperature occurred within earth ( as one of the four so-called `` elements '' ) , others within water , others air , and some more recently within nitre .
Absolute_zero	But all of them seemed to agree that , `` There is some body or other that is of its own nature supremely cold and by participation of which all other bodies obtain that quality . ''
Absolute_zero	The question whether there is a limit to the degree of cold possible , and , if so , where the zero must be placed , was first addressed by the French physicist Guillaume Amontons in 1702 , in connection with his improvements in the air thermometer .
Absolute_zero	In his instrument , temperatures were indicated by the height at which a column of mercury was sustained by a certain mass of air , the volume , or `` spring '' , of which varied with the heat to which it was exposed .
Absolute_zero	Amontons therefore argued that the zero of his thermometer would be that temperature at which the spring of the air in it was reduced to nothing .
Absolute_zero	On the scale he used , the boiling-point of water was marked at +73 and the melting-point of ice at 51 , so that the zero of his scale was equivalent to about − 240 on the Celsius scale .
Absolute_zero	This close approximation to the modern value of − 273.15 ° C for the zero of the air-thermometer was further improved upon in 1779 by Johann Heinrich Lambert , who observed that − 270 ° C might be regarded as absolute cold .
Absolute_zero	Values of this order for the absolute zero were not , however , universally accepted about this period .
Absolute_zero	Pierre-Simon Laplace and Antoine Lavoisier , in their 1780 treatise on heat , arrived at values ranging from 1,500 to 3,000 below the freezing-point of water , and thought that in any case it must be at least 600 below .
Absolute_zero	John Dalton in his Chemical Philosophy gave ten calculations of this value , and finally adopted − 3000 ° C as the natural zero of temperature .
Absolute_zero	After James Prescott Joule had determined the mechanical equivalent of heat , Lord Kelvin approached the question from an entirely different point of view , and in 1848 devised a scale of absolute temperature which was independent of the properties of any particular substance and was based solely on the fundamental laws of thermodynamics .
Absolute_zero	It followed from the principles on which this scale was constructed that its zero was placed at − 273.15 ° C , at almost precisely the same point as the zero of the air-thermometer .
Accent	In linguistics , an accent is a manner of pronunciation peculiar to a particular individual , location , or nation .
Accent	An accent may identify the locality in which its speakers reside ( a geographical or regional accent ) , the socio-economic status of its speakers , their ethnicity , their caste or social class , their first language ( when the language in which the accent is heard is not their native language ) , and so on .
Accent	Accents typically differ in quality of voice , pronunciation of vowels and consonants , stress , and prosody .
Accent	Although grammar , semantics , vocabulary , and other language characteristics often vary concurrently with accent , the word ` accent ' refers specifically to the differences in pronunciation , whereas the word ` dialect ' encompasses the broader set of linguistic differences .
Accent	Often ` accent ' is a subset of ` dialect ' .
Accent	As human beings spread out into isolated communities , stresses and peculiarities develop .
Accent	Over time these can develop into identifiable accents .
Accent	In North America , the interaction of people from many ethnic backgrounds contributed to the formation of the different varieties of North American accents .
Accent	It is difficult to measure or predict how long it takes an accent to formulate .
Accent	Accents in the USA , Canada and Australia , for example , developed from the combinations of different accents and languages in various societies , and the effect of this on the various pronunciations of the British settlers , yet North American accents remain more distant , either as a result of time or of external or `` foreign '' linguistic interaction , such as the Italian accent .
Accent	In many cases , the accents of non-English settlers from the British Isles affected the accents of the different colonies quite differently .
Accent	Irish , Scottish and Welsh immigrants had accents which greatly affected the vowel pronunciation of certain areas of Australia and Canada .
Accent	Children are able to take on accents relatively quickly .
Accent	Children of immigrant families , for example , generally have a more native-like pronunciation than their parents , though both children and parents may have a noticeable non-native accent - however these generally differ : the parents ' accent tends to be influenced by the sound system of their native language whilst the child is more inclined to apply hyper-pronunciation resulting from their need to correct their parents ' shortcomings in fluency .
Accent	Accents seem to remain relatively malleable until a person 's early twenties , after which a person 's accent seems to become more entrenched .
Accent	All the same , accents are not fixed even in adulthood .
Accent	An acoustic analysis by Jonathan Harrington of Elizabeth II 's Royal Christmas Messages revealed that the speech patterns of even so conservative a figure as a monarch can continue to change over her lifetime .
Accent	Pronunciation is the most difficult part of a non-native language to learn .
Accent	Most individuals who speak a non-native language fluently speak it with an accent of their native tongue .
Accent	The most important factor in predicting the degree to which the accent will be noticeable ( or strong ) is the age at which the non-native language was learned .
Accent	The critical period theory states that if learning takes place after the critical period ( usually considered around puberty ) for acquiring native-like pronunciation , an individual is unlikely to acquire a native-like accent .
Accent	This theory , however , is quite controversial among researchers .
Accent	Although many subscribe to some form of the critical period , they either place it earlier than puberty or consider it more of a critical `` window , '' which may vary from one individual to another and depend on factors other than age , such as length of residence , similarity of the non-native language to the native language , and the frequency with which both languages are used .
Accent	Nevertheless , children as young as 6 at the time of moving to another country often speak with a noticeable non-native accent as adults .
Accent	There are also rare instances of individuals who are able to pass for native speakers even if they learned their non-native language in early adulthood .
Accent	However , neurological constrains associated with brain development appear to limit most non-native speakers ' ability to sound native-like .
Accent	Most researchers agree that for adults , acquiring a native-like accent in a non-native language is near impossible .
Accent	When a group defines a standard pronunciation , speakers who deviate from it are often said to `` speak with an accent '' .
Accent	However , everyone speaks with an accent .
Accent	People from the United States would `` speak with an accent '' from the point of view of an Australian , and vice versa .
Accent	Accents such as BBC English or General American or Standard American may sometimes be erroneously designated in their countries of origin as `` accentless '' to indicate that they offer no obvious clue to the speaker 's regional or social background .
Accent	Many teachers of English as a second language neglect to teach speech\/pronunciation .
Accent	Many adult and near-adult learners of second languages have unintelligible speech patterns that may interfere with their education , profession , and social interactions .
Accent	Pronunciation in a second or foreign language involves more than the correct articulation of individual sounds .
Accent	It involves producing a wide range of complex and subtle distinctions which relate sound to meaning at several different levels .
Accent	Teaching of speech\/pronunciation is neglected in part because of the following myths : Pronunciation is n't important : `` This is patently false from any perspective . ''
Accent	Speech\/Pronunciation forms the vehicle for transmitting the speaker 's meaning .
Accent	If the listener does not understand the message , no communication takes place , and although there are other factors involved , one of the most important is the intelligibility of the speaker 's pronunciation .
Accent	Students will pick it up on their own : `` Some will learn to pronounce the second language intelligibly ; many will not . ''
Accent	Inadequate instruction in speech\/pronunciation can result in a complete breakdown in communication .
Accent	The proliferation of commercial `` accent reduction '' services is seen as a sign that many ESL teachers are not meeting their students ' needs for speech\/pronunciation instruction .
Accent	The goals of speech\/pronunciation instruction should include : to help the learner speak in a way that is easy to understand and does not distract the listener , to increase the self-confidence of the learner , and to develop the skills to self-monitor and adapt one 's own speech .
Accent	Even when the listener does understand the speaker , the presence of an accent that is difficult to understand can produce anxiety in the listener that he will not understand what comes next , and cause him to end the conversation earlier or avoid difficult topics .
Accent	Certain accents are perceived to carry more prestige in a society than other accents .
Accent	This is often due to their association with the elite part of society .
Accent	For example in the United Kingdom , Received Pronunciation of the English language is associated with the traditional upper class .
Accent	The same can be said about the predominance of Southeastern Brazilian accents in the case of the Brazilian standard of the Portuguese language , specially considering the disparity of prestige between the most caipira-affected , or rural , speech and the more cultivated paulistano ( Greater São Paulo dialect ) and carioca ( Greater Rio de Janeiro accent ) speakers inside Southeastern Brazil itself .
Accent	However , in linguistics , there is no differentiation among accents in regard to their prestige , aesthetics , or correctness .
Accent	All languages and accents are linguistically equal .
Accent	Stereotypes refer to specific characteristics , traits , and roles that a group and its members are believed to possess .
Accent	Stereotypes can be both positive and negative , although negative are more common .
Accent	Stereotypes may result in prejudice , which is defined as having negative attitudes toward a group and its members .
Accent	Individuals with non-standard accents often have to deal with both negative stereotypes and prejudice because of an accent .
Accent	Researchers consistently show that people with accents are judged as less intelligent , less competent , less educated , having poor English\/language skills , and unpleasant to listen to .
Accent	Not only people with standard accents subscribe to these beliefs and attitudes , but individuals with accents also often stereotype against their own or others ' accents .
Accent	Discrimination refers to specific behaviors or actions directed at a group or its individual members based solely on the group membership .
Accent	In accent discrimination , one 's way of speaking is used as a basis for arbitrary evaluations and judgments .
Accent	Unlike other forms of discrimination , there are no strong norms against accent discrimination in the general society .
Accent	Rosina Lippi-Green writes , Speakers with certain accents often experience discrimination in housing and employment .
Accent	For example , landlords are less likely to call back speakers who have foreign or ethnic accents and are more likely to be assigned by employers to lower status positions than are those with standard accents .
Accent	In business settings , individuals with non-standard accents are more likely to be evaluated negatively .
Accent	Accent discrimination is also present in educational institutions .
Accent	For example , non-native speaking graduate students , lecturers , and professors , across college campuses in the US have been target for being unintelligible because of accent .
Accent	On average , however , students taught by non-native English speakers do not underperform when compared to those taught by native speakers of English .
Accent	Studies have shown the perception of the accent , not the accent by itself , often results in negative evaluations of speakers .
Accent	In a study conducted by Rubin ( 1992 ) , students listened to a taped lecture recorded by the same native English speaker with a standard accent .
Accent	However , they were shown a picture of the lecturer who was either a Caucasian or Asian .
Accent	Participants in the study who saw the Asian picture believed that they had heard an accented lecturer and performed more badly on a task measuring lecture comprehension .
Accent	Negative evaluations may reflect the prejudices rather than real issues with understanding accents .
Accent	In the United States , Title VII of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 prohibits discrimination based on national origin , implying accents .
Accent	However , employers may claim that a person 's accent impairs his or her communication skills that are necessary to the effective business operation .
Accent	The courts often rely on the employer 's claims or use judges ' subjective opinions when deciding whether the ( potential ) employee 's accent would interfere with communication or performance , without any objective proof that accent was or might be a hindrance .
Accent	Kentucky 's highest court in the case of Clifford vs. Commonwealth held that a white police officer , who had not seen the black defendant allegedly involved in a drug transaction , could , nevertheless , identify him as a participant by saying that a voice on an audiotape `` sounded black . ''
Accent	The police officer based this `` identification '' on the fact that the defendant was the only African American man in the room at the time of the transaction and that an audio-tape contained the voice of a man the officer said `` sounded black '' selling crack cocaine to a white informant planted by the police .
Accent	Actors are often called upon to speak varieties of language other than their own .
Accent	For example , American actor Dick van Dyke attempted to imitate a British accent in the film Mary Poppins .
Accent	Similarly , an actor may portray a character of some nationality other than his or her own by adopting into the native language the phonological profile typical of the nationality to be portrayed - what is commonly called `` speaking with an accent '' .
Accent	One example would be Viggo Mortensen 's use of a Russian accent in his portrayal of Nikolai in the movie Eastern Promises .
Accent	Accents may have associations and implications for an audience .
Accent	For example , in Disney films from the 1990s onward , English accents are generally employed to serve one of two purposes : slapstick comedy or evil genius .
Accent	Examples include Aladdin ( the Sultan and Jafar , respectively ) , The Lion King ( Zazu and Scar , respectively ) , The Hunchback of Notre Dame ( Victor the Gargoyle and Frollo , respectively ) , and Pocahontas ( Wiggins and Ratcliffe , respectively - both of whom happen to be played by the same actor , American David Ogden Stiers ) .
Angers	Coordinates : 47 ° 28 ′ 25 ″ N 0 ° 33 ′ 15 ″ W \/ 47.4736 ° N 0.5542 ° W \/ 47.4736 ; -0.5542 Angers ( French pronunciation : ( ɑ̃ .
Angers	ʒe ) ) is the main city in the Maine-et-Loire department in western France about 300 km ( 190 mi ) south-west of Paris .
Angers	Angers is located in the French region known by its pre-revolutionary , provincial name , Anjou , and its inhabitants are called Angevins .
Angers	Angers proper has a population of 157,000 inhabitants , while c. 283,000 live in its metropolitan area .
Angers	The city traces its roots to early Roman times .
Angers	It occupies both banks of the Maine , which is spanned by six bridges .
Angers	The district along the river has flourishing nurseries and market gardens .
Angers	It is known for its fresh produce and cut flowers .
Angers	The first sign of human presence on the site of Angers is a stone tool dated back to 400,000 BCE ( Lower Paleolithic ) .
Angers	The earliest known inhabitants were the Andecavi , a Gallic tribe that was overrun by the Romans .
Angers	The city , while under Roman rule , was called Juliomagus .
Angers	The Council of Angers was held here in 453 .
Angers	The city suffered severely from the invasions of the Vikings in 845 and succeeding years .
Angers	Angers was once the capital of the historic province of Anjou .
Angers	Beginning in the 9th century , the region was controlled by a powerful family of feudal lords .
Angers	It is the cradle of the House of Plantagenet who ruled England from the twelfth century and gave name to the Angevin Kings of England .
Angers	During this time the Hospital of Saint-Jean was built in Angers by King Henry II of England .
Angers	The edifice still stands to this day , now housing an important museum .
Angers	In 1204 Angers was conquered by King Philippe II .
Angers	An enormous castle , the Château d'Angers , was built during the minority of Louis IX ( `` Saint Louis '' ) in the early part of the 13th century .
Angers	In 1352 , John II le Bon , gave the château to his son , Louis I. Married to the daughter of the wealthy Duke of Brittany , Louis I had the château modified , and in 1373 commissioned the famous Apocalypse Tapestry from the painter Hennequin de Bruges and the Parisian tapestry-weaver Nicolas Bataille .
Angers	In the early 15th century , the dauphin who became King Charles VII , had to flee Paris and was given sanctuary at the Château D'Angers .
Angers	Louis II and Yolande d'Aragon added a chapel ( 1405-12 ) and royal apartments to the castle .
Angers	The chapel is a sainte chapelle , the name given to churches which enshrined a relic of the Passion .
Angers	The relic at Angers was a splinter of the fragment of the True Cross which had been acquired by Louis IX .
Angers	The Huguenots took the city of Angers in 1585 , and the Vendean royalists were defeated nearby in 1793 during the siege of Angers .
Angers	Until the French Revolution Angers was the seat of a celebrated university founded in the 14th century .
Angers	During the 16th and 17th centuries the Château D'Angers served originally as a defensive castle , and later as a military training school .
Angers	The military role of the Chateau D'Angers castle was revived in the 20th century when it was used by the Nazi government of Germany to store arms , ammunition , and explosives .
Angers	During the war , the latter exploded , causing significant amounts of damage to the castle .
Angers	In addition to the massive Château d'Angers , the city is also noted for the impressive twin spires of the twelfth-century Cathedral of Saint-Maurice .
Angers	Other noteworthy churches around Angers include St. Serge , an abbey-church of the 12th and 15th centuries , and the twelfth-century La Trinité Cathedral .
Angers	The elaborately sculptured eleventh and 12th century arcades of the famous abbey of Saint Aubin survive in the courtyard of the Prefecture and Hotel du Departement .
Angers	The tower of the abbey church has also survived nearby .
Angers	Ruins of the old churches of Toussaint ( 13th century ) and Notre-Dame du Ronceray ( eleventh century ) are also nearby .
Angers	The ancient hospital of St. Jean ( twelfth century ) is occupied by Jean Lurcat 's tapestries .
Angers	The Logis Barrault , a mansion built in 1486-92 , houses the Musée des Beaux-Arts , which has a large collection of paintings and sculptures .
Angers	In 1984 the former abbey church of Toussaint became the Musee David d'Angers consisting of works by the sculptor David d'Angers , who was a native of the town .
Angers	In the middle of a main boulevard near the museum stands his bronze statue of René of Anjou , who was born in the chateau of Angers .
Angers	The Hôtel de Pincé or d'Anjou ( 1523-1530 ) is the finest of the stone mansions of Angers .
Angers	There are also many curious wooden houses of the fifteenth and 16th centuries .
Angers	The Palais de Justice , the Catholic Institute , a fine theater , and a hospital with 1500 beds are the more remarkable of the modern buildings of the town .
Angers	Angers is the seat of a bishopric , dating from the 3rd century ; a prefecture ; a court of appeal ; and a court of assizes ( criminal courts ) .
Angers	It has a tribunal of first instance , a tribunal of commerce , a board of trade-arbitrators , a chamber of commerce , a branch of the Bank of France , and several learned societies .
Angers	The early prosperity of the town is largely due to the nearby quarries of slate , whose abundant use for the roofs of Angers led to the city 's nickname , the `` Black City '' ( or `` La ville noire '' , in French ) .
Angers	As of 1911 , existing industries noted in the Encyclopædia Britannica for that year included the distillation of liqueurs from fruit ( Cointreau , a brand of triple sec orange liqueur , is produced to this day in Saint-Barthélemy-d'Anjou , a suburb of Angers ) ; cable , rope , and thread-making ; the manufacture of boots , shoes , umbrellas , and parasols ; weaving of sail-cloth and fabrics ; machine construction ; wire-drawing ; and the manufacture of sparkling wines and preserved fruits .
Angers	The chief articles of commerce , besides slate and manufactured goods , were hemp , early vegetables , fruit , flowers , and live-stock .
Angers	Many of these industries in 1911 have since disappeared , though Cointreau continues to produce liqueur .
Angers	Other contemporary industries include the manufacturing of lorries ( Scania ) and computers ( Bull , Packard-Bell , NEC ) as well as research in horticulture and biotechnologies .
Angers	Angers is connected by A11 autoroute to Paris ( c. 295 km ) and to Nantes ( c. 90 km ) .
Angers	Gare d'Angers-Saint-Laud railway station has a direct TGV service to Paris ( 1 hour 35 minutes ) .
Angers	The nearest airport is Angers - Loire Airport .
Angers	In 1850 a catastrophic failure of the Angers Bridge caused the deaths of over 200 soldiers .
Angers	The disaster inhibited the construction of suspension bridges in France for two decades .
Angers	Angers inaugurated a new light rail system on 25 June 2011 .
Angers	The tramway consists of one 12 km ( 7.46 mi ) line with 25 stops .
Angers	The line runs from Avrillé-Ardenne in the North to Angers-Roseraie in the south .
Angers	Service is provided by Keolis using 17 Alstom Citadis trams .
Angers	Angers has an orchestra , ONPL ( Orchestre National des Pays de la Loire ) , shared with Nantes , a local theater NTA ( Nouveau Théatre d'Angers ) and a dance school CNDC ( Centre National de Danse Contemporaine ) .
Angers	Angers has a few important museums on the national level : `` Musée des Beaux-Arts '' ( Art & Sculpture , the permanent collections : 14th to the present ) has just reopened , after five years of work .
Angers	`` Galerie David d'Angers '' , which is consecrated to the 19th century sculptor David d'Angers .
Angers	`` Musée Pincé '' , which holds a collection of Classical art , as well as Egyptian , Etruscan , Japanese and Chinese .
Angers	`` Musée Jean Lurçat et de la Tapisserie contemporaine '' , is a tapestry museum .
Angers	The famous tapestry series `` Le chant du Monde '' by Jean Lurçat is in the ancient Hôpital St-Jean , the oldest hospital in France , while another modern building holds the contemporary collections , and also other works by Jean Lurçat .
Angers	The Apocalypse Tapestry , or `` the tapestries of the Apocalypse '' , originally made for Louis I d'Anjou in the fourteenth century , are today in the Château d'Angers after their restoration .
Angers	Muséum d'histoire naturelle d'Angers is an important natural history museum in the `` Hôtel Demarie-Valentin '' , dating from 1521 .
Angers	Angers is an important center for tapestries , especially contemporary tapestry .
Angers	It calls itself the `` most flowered city in Europe '' , and its displays of live and cut flowers are stunning .
Angers	The city 's Jardin des Plantes d'Angers and Jardin botanique de la Faculté de Pharmacie d'Angers are a historic botanical gardens , and its Arboretum Gaston Allard is a major arboretum .
Angers	It is also well known for being the seat of important cultural events , such as the film festival Premiers Plans , Tour de Scènes ( free concerts in the streets ) and Les Accroche-Coeurs ( free street festival ) .
Angers	Angers has many sport teams playing at top levels : Angers SCO is Angers 's football team .
Angers	The club was created in 1919 .
Angers	In 2010-11 season , Angers SCO is playing in the Ligue 2 ( second division ) league .
Angers	Les Ducs d'Angers is Angers 's ice hockey team .
Angers	The club is playing in the Magnus League ( first division ) .
Angers	Anjou BC is Angers 's basketball team , playing in second division .
Angers	Angers acts as home to the Angers Aviron Nautique ( In French ) , a rowing club which actively competes in regattas across France .
Angers	A center of learning , Angers boasts two renowned universities and several specialized institutions , altogether responsible for more than 26,000 students .
Angers	The city has a Catholic university , the Université Catholique de L'Ouest ( Catholic University of the West , or UCO ) , one of five Catholic universities in France .
Angers	UCO is best known for its French language studies institute , the Centre international d'étude de la langue française ( CIDEF ) , which provides college students from around the world with college-level course instruction in the French language .
Angers	The town is also home to a state university , the University of Angers .
Angers	Angers 's other educational institutions include lycées ; training colleges , an engineering school in manufacturing ( ENSAM ) , an engineering school in electronics and computer science ( ESEO ) , and a school of fine art .
Angers	Its education and research institutes are the driving force behind the city 's science and technology industries .
Angers	Angers 's Business School is ESSCA ( Ecole Superieure des Sciences Commerciales d'Angers ) .
Angers	Formerly part of the UCO , the school 's Masters program is of a duration of five years .
Angers	ESSCA is recruiting students after the Baccalaureat .
Angers	In addition to French schools and universities , an American university St. Edward 's University has new expanding campus in Angers .
Angers	St. Edward 's University is a diverse , Catholic liberal arts institution from Austin , TX .
Angers	The university has a partnership with UCO , and offers a variety of courses of undergraduate level and professional training .
Angers	The city operates the Toussaint Main Library and nine branch libraries .
Angers	The city is the birthplace of : René I of Naples ( 1409-1480 ) Jean Bodin ( 1529-1596 ) , philosopher and jurist , author of Six Livres de la République .
Angers	Michel Eugène Chevreul , ( 1786-1889 ) , chemist .
Angers	Joseph Louis Proust , ( 1754-1826 ) , chemist responsible for `` Proust 's law '' Pierre-Jean David d'Angers , ( 1788-1856 ) , sculptor .
Angers	Prosper Ménière ( 1799-1862 ) , physician .
Angers	Édouard Cointreau , ( 1849-1923 ) , creator of the `` Cointreau '' orange-flavoured liquor .
Angers	René Bazin ( 1853-1932 ) , writer and educator .
Angers	Fernand Charron ( 1866-1921 ) , one of the first cars constructors ( Octave Mirbeau dedicated to Charron La 628-E8 , 1907 ) .
Angers	André Bazin ( 1918-1958 ) , critic of the French New Wave .
Angers	Hervé Bazin ( 1911-1996 ) , writer .
Angers	Henri Dutilleux ( born 1916 ) , composer .
Angers	Joseph Wresinski ( born 1917 ) , humanitarian activist .
Angers	Paul Poupard ( born 1930 ) , Roman Catholic cardinal .
Angers	Jacques Loussier ( born 1934 ) , composer and jazz pianist .
Angers	Francis Le Jau , ( 1665-1717 ) , Anglican missionary to West Indies and South Carolina , worked for the humane treatment of slaves .
Angers	Nicolas Mahut ( born 1982 ) , tennis player .
Angers	Juliana Mialoundama , basketball player .
Angers	Eriq Ebouaney ( Born 1967 ) , actor .
Angers	Angers is twinned with : Haarlem , Netherlands , since 1964 .
Angers	Osnabrück , Germany , since 1964 .
Angers	Bamako , Mali , since 1974 .
Angers	Pisa , Italy , since 1982 .
Angers	Wigan , United Kingdom , since 1988 .
Angers	Södertälje , Sweden , since 1998 .
Angers	Seville , Spain , since 2000 .
Angers	Yantai , China , since 2006 .
Angers	Austin , Texas , USA , since 2011 .
Actor	An actor ( sometimes actress for female ; see terminology ) is a person who acts in a dramatic or comic production and who works in film , television , theater , or radio in that capacity .
Actor	After 1660 , when women first appeared on stage , actor and actress were initially used interchangeably for female performers , but later , influenced by the French actrice , actress became the usual term .
Actor	The etymology is a simple derivation from actor with ess added .
Actor	The word actor refers to a person who acts regardless of gender , and this term `` is increasingly preferred '' , while actress refers specifically to a female person who acts .
Actor	Actress `` remains in general use '' , although in a survey of a `` wide cross-section of current British English '' , compiled in 2010 , actor was almost twice as commonly found as actress .
Actor	Within the profession , however , the re-adoption of the neutral term dates to the 1950s-60s , the post-war period when women 's contribution to cultural life in general was being re-evaluated .
Actor	Actress remains the common term used in major acting awards given to female recipients .
Actor	The gender-neutral term `` player '' was common in film in the early days of the Motion Picture Production Code with regards to the cinema of the United States , but is now generally deemed archaic .
Actor	However , it remains in use in the theater , often incorporated into the name of a theater group or company ( such as the East West Players ) .
Actor	The first recorded case of an actor performing took place in 534 BC ( though the changes in calendar over the years make it hard to determine exactly ) when the Greek performer Thespis stepped on to the stage at the Theatre Dionysus and became the first known person to speak words as a character in a play or story .
Actor	Prior to Thespis ' act , stories were only known to be told in song and dance and in third person narrative .
Actor	In honor of Thespis , actors are commonly called Thespians .
Actor	Theatrical legend to this day maintains that Thespis exists as a mischievous spirit , and disasters in the theater are sometimes blamed on his ghostly intervention .
Actor	Actors were traditionally not people of high status , and in the Early Middle Ages traveling acting troupes were often viewed with distrust .
Actor	In many parts of Europe , actors could not even receive a Christian burial , and traditional beliefs of the region and time period held that this left any actor forever condemned .
Actor	However , this negative perception was largely reversed in the 19th and 20th centuries as acting has become an honored and popular profession and art .
Actor	Method acting is a technique developed from the acting ` system ' created in the early 20th century by Konstantin Stanislavski in his work at the Moscow Art Theatre and its studios .
Actor	The Group Theatre first popularized the Method in the 1930s ; it was subsequently advanced and developed in new directions by Stella Adler , Sanford Meisner , Uta Hagen , Lee Strasberg ( at the Actors Studio in the 1940s and 50s ) , and others .
Actor	In Stanislavski 's system ' , the actor analyzes the character in order to play him or her with psychological realism and emotional authenticity .
Actor	Using the Method , an actor may recall emotions or reactions from his or her own life and use them to identify with the character being portrayed .
Actor	Method actors are often characterized as immersing themselves so totally in their characters that they continue to portray them even off-stage or off-camera for the duration of the project .
Actor	However , this is a popular misconception .
Actor	While some actors do employ this approach , it is generally not taught as part of the Method .
Actor	Stella Adler , who was a member of the Group Theatre , along with Strasberg , emphasised a different approach of using creative imagination .
Actor	Method acting offers a systematic form of actor training in which the actor 's sensory , psychological , and emotional abilities are developed ; it revolutionized theater in the United States .
Actor	Presentational acting refers to a relationship between actor and audience , whether by direct address or indirectly by specific use of language , looks , gestures or other signs indicating that the character or actor is aware of the audience 's presence .
Actor	( Shakespeare 's use of punning and wordplay , for example , often has this function of indirect contact . )
Actor	In representational acting , `` actors want to make us ` believe ' they are the character ; they pretend . ''
Actor	The illusion of the fourth wall with the audience as voyeurs is striven for .
Actor	In the past , only men could become actors in some societies .
Actor	In the ancient Greece and Rome and the medieval world , it was considered disgraceful for a woman to go on the stage , and this belief persisted until the 17th century , when in Venice it was broken .
Actor	In the time of William Shakespeare , women 's roles were generally played by men or boys .
Actor	When an eighteen-year Puritan prohibition of drama was lifted after the English Restoration of 1660 , women began to appear on stage in England .
Actor	Margaret Hughes is credited by some as the first professional actress on the English stage .
Actor	This prohibition ended during the reign of Charles II in part due to the fact that he enjoyed watching actresses on stage .
Actor	The first occurrence of the term actress was in 1700 according to the OED and is ascribed to Dryden .
Actor	In Japan , men ( onnagata ) took over the female roles in kabuki theater when women were banned from performing on stage during the Edo period .
Actor	This convention has continued to the present .
Actor	However , some forms of Chinese drama have women playing all the roles .
Actor	In modern times , women sometimes play the roles of prepubescent boys .
Actor	The stage role of Peter Pan , for example , is traditionally played by a woman , as are most principal boys in British pantomime .
Actor	Opera has several `` breeches roles '' traditionally sung by women , usually mezzo-sopranos .
Actor	Examples are Hansel in Hänsel und Gretel , Cherubino in The Marriage of Figaro and Octavian in Der Rosenkavalier .
Actor	Women in male roles are uncommon in film with the notable exceptions of the films The Year of Living Dangerously and I 'm Not There .
Actor	In the former film Linda Hunt played the pivotal role of Billy Kwan , for which she received the Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress .
Actor	In the latter film Cate Blanchett portrayed Jude Quinn , a representation of Bob Dylan in the sixties , for which she was nominated for the Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress .
Actor	Women playing men in live theater is particularly common in presentations of older plays , such as those of Shakespeare , that have large numbers of male characters in roles where the gender no longer matters in modern times .
Actor	Having an actor dress as the opposite sex for comic effect is also a long-standing tradition in comic theater and film .
Actor	Most of Shakespeare 's comedies include instances of overt cross-dressing , such as Francis Flute in A Midsummer Night 's Dream .
Actor	The movie A Funny Thing Happened on the Way to the Forum stars Jack Gilford dressing as a young bride .
Actor	Tony Curtis and Jack Lemmon famously posed as women to escape gangsters in the Billy Wilder film Some Like It Hot .
Actor	Cross-dressing for comic effect was a frequently used device in most of the thirty Carry On films .
Actor	Dustin Hoffman and Robin Williams have each appeared in a hit comedy film ( Tootsie and Mrs. Doubtfire , respectively ) in which they played most scenes dressed as a woman .
Actor	Occasionally , the issue is further complicated , for example , by a woman playing a woman acting as a man pretending to be a woman , like Julie Andrews in Victor\/Victoria , or Gwyneth Paltrow in Shakespeare in Love .
Actor	In It 's Pat : The Movie , filmwatchers never learn the gender of the androgynous main characters Pat and Chris ( played by Julia Sweeney and Dave Foley ) .
Actor	A few roles in modern films , plays and musicals are played by a member of the opposite sex ( rather than a character cross-dressing ) , such as the character Edna Turnblad in Hairspray-played by Divine in the original film , Harvey Fierstein in the Broadway musical , and John Travolta in the 2007 movie musical .
Actor	Linda Hunt won an Academy Award for Best Supporting Actress for playing Billy Kwan in The Year of Living Dangerously .
Actor	Felicity Huffman was nominated for an Academy Award for Best Actress for playing Bree Osbourne ( a male-to-female transsexual ) in Transamerica .
Azuki_bean	The azuki bean ( アズキ （ 小豆 ） , azuki ?
Azuki_bean	, also spelled adzuki or aduki ) is an annual vine , Vigna angularis , widely grown throughout East Asia and the Himalayas for its small ( approximately 5 mm ) bean .
Azuki_bean	The cultivars most familiar in Northeast Asia have a uniform red color .
Azuki_bean	However , white , black , gray and variously mottled varieties are also known .
Azuki_bean	Scientists presume Vigna angularis var .
Azuki_bean	nipponensis is the progenitor .
Azuki_bean	Genetic evidence indicates that the azuki bean was first domesticated in East Asia and later crossbred with native species in Himalayas .
Azuki_bean	The bean was first unearthed at Awazu-kotei Ruin of Japanese mid Jōmon period in 4000BC , and later it was commonly found on many Jomon ruins in 4000BC to 2000BC in Japan .
Azuki_bean	The analysis of the unearthed beans indicates that it was first cultivated in Japan during 4000BC to 2000BC .
Azuki_bean	In China and Korea it was first found on the ruins in 3000BC to 1000BC , and these are thought to be cultivated ones .
Azuki_bean	Some Koreans insist that it was first cultivated on the Korean peninsula before 1000 BC and later taken to Japan , where it is now the second most popular legume after the soybean .
Azuki_bean	The name azuki is a transliteration of the native Japanese name .
Azuki_bean	Japanese also has a Chinese loanword , shōzu ( 小豆 ? )
Azuki_bean	, which means `` small bean '' , its counterpart `` large bean '' ( 大豆 , daizu ? )
Azuki_bean	being the soybean .
Azuki_bean	In China , the corresponding name ( Chinese : 小豆 ; pinyin : xiǎodòu ) is still used in botanical or agricultural parlance .
Azuki_bean	However in everyday Chinese , the more common terms are hongdou ( 紅豆 ; hóngdòu ) and chidou ( 赤豆 ; chìdòu ) , both meaning `` red bean '' , because almost all Chinese cultivars are uniformly red .
Azuki_bean	In English-language discussions of Chinese topics , the term `` red bean '' is often used ( especially in reference to red bean paste ) , but in other contexts this usage can cause confusion with other beans that are also red .
Azuki_bean	In normal contexts , `` red cowpeas '' have been used to refer to this bean .
Azuki_bean	In some parts of India , they are referred to as `` Red Chori '' .
Azuki_bean	In Indian Punjab it is called `` ravaa ` n '' and is a common ingredient of chaat .
Azuki_bean	In Marathi , it is known as Lal Chavali ( लाल चवळी ) - literally means ` red cowpea ' .
Azuki_bean	In East Asian cuisine , the azuki bean is commonly eaten sweetened .
Azuki_bean	In particular , it is often boiled with sugar , resulting in red bean paste ( an ) , a very common ingredient in all of these cuisines .
Azuki_bean	It is also common to add flavoring to the bean paste , such as chestnut .
Azuki_bean	Red bean paste is used in many Chinese foods , such as tangyuan , zongzi , mooncakes , baozi and red bean ice .
Azuki_bean	It is also serves as a filling for Japanese sweets like anpan , dorayaki , imagawayaki , manjū , monaka , anmitsu , taiyaki and daifuku .
Azuki_bean	A more liquid version , using azuki beans boiled with sugar and a pinch of salt , produces a sweet dish called red bean soup .
Azuki_bean	Azuki beans are also commonly eaten sprouted , or boiled in a hot , tea-like drink .
Azuki_bean	Some Asian cultures enjoy red bean paste as a filling or topping for various kinds of waffles , pastries , baked buns or biscuits .
Azuki_bean	In Japan , rice with azuki beans ( 赤飯 ; sekihan ) is traditionally cooked for auspicious occasions .
Azuki_bean	Azuki beans are also used to produce amanattō , and as a popular flavor of ice cream .
Azuki_bean	On October 20 , 2009 , Pepsi Japan released an azuki-flavored Pepsi product .
Azuki_bean	Azuki beans , along with butter and sugar , form the basis of the popular Somali supper dish cambuulo .
Azuki_bean	In Gujarat , India , they are known as chori .
Azuki_bean	Azuki beans are a good source for a variety of minerals , with 1 cup of cooked beans providing 4.6 mg of Iron ( ~ 25 % RDI ) , 119.6 mg of magnesium ( ~ 30 % RDI ) , 1.223 g of potassium ( ~ 25 % AI ) , 4.0 mg of zinc ( ~ 25 % RDI ) and 278 µg of folic acid ( ~ 70 % RDI ) .
Atrax	`` Atrax '' redirects here .
Atrax	For the mythological figure , see Atrax ( mythology ) .
Atrax	Atracinae , commonly known as Australian funnel-web spiders , is a subfamily of spiders in the funnel-web spider family Hexathelidae .
Atrax	Atracinae consists of three genera : Atrax , Hadronyche , and Illawarra .
Atrax	The subfamily includes species with medically significant venom , the most well-known of which is the Sydney funnel-web spider ( Atrax robustus ) .
Atrax	There have been no fatalities since the introduction of modern first aid techniques and antivenin .
Atrax	These spiders are medium-to-large in size , with body lengths ranging from 1 cm to 5 cm ( 0.4 '' to 2 '' ) .
Atrax	They are darkly colored , ranging from black to blue-black to plum to brown , with a glossy , hairless carapace covering the front part of the body .
Atrax	Like the related diplurid spiders , some hexathelids have relatively long spinnerets ; this is especially true of A. robustus .
Atrax	Like other Mygalomorphae ( also incorrectly called `` Orthognatha '' ) - an infraorder of spiders that includes the tropical tarantulas - these spiders have fangs which point straight down the body and do not point towards each other ( cf Araneomorphae ) .
Atrax	They have ample venom glands that lie entirely within their chelicerae .
Atrax	Their fangs are large and powerful , capable of penetrating fingernails and soft shoes .
Atrax	Funnel-webs make their burrows in moist , cool , sheltered habitats-under rocks , in and under rotting logs , some in rough-barked trees ( occasionally metres above ground ) .
Atrax	They are commonly found in suburban rockeries and shrubberies , rarely in lawns or other open terrain .
Atrax	A funnel-web 's burrow characteristically has irregular silk trip-lines radiating from the entrance .
Atrax	Unlike some related trapdoor spiders , funnel-webs do not build lids to their burrows .
Atrax	The primary range of the Australian funnel-web spiders is the eastern coast of Australia , with specimens found in New South Wales , South Australia , Victoria , and Queensland .
Atrax	The only Australian states without funnel-webs are Western Australia and the Northern Territory .
Atrax	Australian funnel-webs are one of the three most dangerous spiders in the world and are regarded by some to be the most dangerous .
Atrax	Examination of bite records has implicated wandering males in most if not all fatal funnel-web bites to humans .
Atrax	Adult males , recognized by the modified terminal segment of the palp , will defend themselves vigorously if they feel threatened and tend to wander during the warmer months of the year looking for receptive females for mating .
Atrax	They are attracted to water and hence are often found in swimming pools , into which they often fall while wandering .
Atrax	The spiders can survive such immersion for several hours and can deliver a bite when removed from the water .
Atrax	They also show up in garages and yards in suburban Sydney .
Atrax	Contrary to a commonly held belief , no funnel-web spider is able to jump , although they can run quickly .
Atrax	While some very venomous spiders may give dry bites , these spiders do so much less frequently .
Atrax	An inefficient mode of delivery ( to large animals ) and interrupted contact are also possible causes of low volume delivery .
Atrax	It has been claimed that approximately 10 % to 25 % of bites will produce significant toxicity but the likelihood can not be predicted and all should be treated as potentially life-threatening .
Atrax	Funnel-webs are not normally aggressive but will defend themselves vigorously if frightened or threatened .
Atrax	During an attack the funnel-web spider generally maintains a tight grip on its victim and bites repeatedly , making it an especially traumatic experience for humans who are bitten and increasing the risk of severe envenomation .
Atrax	There have been 27 recorded deaths in Australia in the last 100 years from spider bites .
Atrax	Bites from Sydney funnel-web spiders have caused thirteen deaths ( seven in children ) .
Atrax	In all cases where the sex of the biting spider could be determined , it was found to be the male of the species .
Atrax	Most victims were young , ill or infirm .
Atrax	One member of the genus Hadronyche , the northern tree funnel-web has also been claimed to cause fatal envenomation but , to date , this lacks the support of a specific medical report .
Atrax	Assays of venom from several Hadronyche species have shown it to be similar to Atrax venom .
Atrax	There are many different toxins in the venom of Atrax and Hadronyche spiders .
Atrax	Collectively , these spider toxins are given the name atracotoxins ( ACTX ) , as all these spiders belong to the subfamily Atracinae .
Atrax	The first toxins isolated were the δ-ACTX toxins present in the venom of both A. robustus ( δ-ACTX-Ar1 , formerly known as robustoxin or atracotoxin ) and H. versuta ( δ-ACTX-Hv1a , formerly known as versutotoxin ) .
Atrax	Both these toxins produce the same funnel-web envenoming syndrome in monkeys as that seen in humans , suggesting that they are responsible for the physiological effects seen with crude venom .
Atrax	These toxins are thought to operate by opening sodium channels .
Atrax	They are presynaptic neurotoxins that ( via sodium channels ) induce spontaneous , repetitive firing of action potentials in autonomic and motor neurons and inhibit neurally mediated transmitted release resulting in a surge of endogenous acetylcholine , noradrenaline and adrenaline .
Atrax	Although extremely toxic to primates , the venom appears to be fairly harmless to many other animals .
Atrax	It has been suggested that these animals may be resistant to the venom 's effects due to the presence of IgG , and possibly cross-linked IgG and IgM inactivating factors in their blood plasma that bind to the toxins responsible and neutralise them .
Atrax	The female venom was thought to be only about a sixth as potent to humans as that of the male The bite of a female or juvenile may still be serious ; however , considerable variability occurs in venom toxicity between species , together with assumable degrees of inefficiency in the method of venom delivery .
Atrax	Envenomation symptoms observed following bites by these spiders are very similar .
Atrax	The bite is initially very painful , due to the biochemical action of the venom and the size of the fangs penetrating the skin .
Atrax	Puncture marks and local bleeding are also usually visible .
Atrax	If substantial envenomation occurs , symptoms will generally occur within minutes and progress rapidly .
Atrax	Early symptoms of systemic envenomation include goose bumps , sweating , tingling around the mouth and tongue , twitching ( initially facial and intercostal ) , salivation , watery eyes , elevated heart rate and elevated blood pressure .
Atrax	As systemic envenomation progresses symptoms include nausea , vomiting , shortness of breath ( caused by airway obstruction ) , agitation , confusion , writhing , grimacing , muscle spasms , pulmonary oedema ( of neurogenic or hypertensive origin ) , metabolic acidosis and extreme hypertension .
Atrax	The final stages of severe envenomation include dilation of the pupils ( often fixed ) , uncontrolled generalised muscle twitching , unconsciousness , elevated intracranial pressure and death .
Atrax	When death occurs it is generally as a result of progressive hypotension or possibly elevated intracranial pressure consequent on cerebral oedema .
Atrax	The onset of severe envenomation can be rapid .
Atrax	In one prospective study , the median time to onset of envenomation was 28 minutes , with only two cases having onset after 2 hours ( both had pressure immobilisation bandages applied ) .
Atrax	Death may occur within a period ranging from 15 minutes ( this occurred when a small child was bitten ) to three days .
Atrax	Due to the severity of symptoms , and the speed with which they progress , in areas where these spiders are known to live all bites from large black spiders should be treated as though they were caused by a funnel-web spider .
Atrax	First aid treatment for a suspected funnel-web spider bite consists of immediately applying a pressure immobilisation bandage ; a technique which consists of wrapping the bitten limb with a crepe bandage , as well as applying a splint to limit movement of the limb .
