Australia_national_football_team	Archie Thompson , the Australian forward and number 20 , scored an amazing 13 goals in Nicky Salapu 's goal in the 12th , 23rd , 27th , 29th , 32nd , 37th , 42nd , 45th , 56th , 60th , 65th , 85th and 88th minutes , with unexpected mistakes by Nicky , even though saving many hard shots from the Australian players , some of them from the first 10 minutes of the game .
Australia_national_football_team	The Australian national team first played at the World Cup finals in West Germany in 1974 after having missed out in play-offs in 1966 and 1970 , losing to North Korea and Israel respectively .
Australia_national_football_team	The road to the 1974 World Cup began with a series of home and away matches against Iraq , New Zealand , and Indonesia .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos , having won this tournament , then played and won a two-legged fixture against one of the Socceroos ' biggest rivals Iran , managing to hold on to a slim overall lead in front of 120,000 Iranian fans in the Azadi Stadium , Tehran , during the second leg .
Australia_national_football_team	South Korea , having itself knocked out Israel at the equivalent stage , was then drawn as Australia 's final hurdle .
Australia_national_football_team	Over the course of another two-legged playoff the scores remained even , and so a deciding match was played in Hong Kong .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia won this match , through a Jimmy Mackay goal , scored off a free kick .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia were drawn into Group A consisting of hosts and favorites West Germany , East Germany and Chile .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia held the East German 's 0-0 at half-time before defender Colin Curran deflected the ball into his own net early in the second half .
Australia_national_football_team	East German striker Joachim Streich then secured the points with a goal half-way through the second half , with the game finishing 2-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia lost their following match to West Germany 3-0 with goals to Wolfgang Overath , Bernhard Cullmann and star-striker Gerd Müller .
Australia_national_football_team	Having lost both their opening games , Australia could not proceed further in the tournament and the Australians managed to hold Chile to a scoreless draw , seeing Australia earn its first ever World Cup finals point .
Australia_national_football_team	It was to be the last appearance for the Australian team until the World Cup tournament returned to Germany more than three decades later .
Australia_national_football_team	Over that 32 year time span , the Australian team was known for its near misses in its attempts to qualify for the FIFA World Cup , most notably 1998 against Iran and 2002 against Uruguay .
Australia_national_football_team	Before that , they lost play-offs in 1966 ( to North Korea ) , 1970 ( to Israel ) , 1986 ( to Scotland ) , and 1994 ( to Argentina ) and even lost to Fiji in the OFC qualifying matches in 1988 1-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's road to USA 94 is an example of the difficult qualifying path which members of the Oceania confederation have had to endure .
Australia_national_football_team	In order to qualify for USA 94 , Australia had to endure 3 playoff stages .
Australia_national_football_team	The first stage was the Oceania playoff .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia finished on top of Group 1 in Oceania going undefeated in four games against weaker sides Tahiti and the Solomon Islands and scoring thirteen goals over the four games .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia played New Zealand in the Oceania playoff .
Australia_national_football_team	The first leg was played in New Zealand on 30 May 1993 , with Australia winning the game 1-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia won the return leg 3-0 to win the playoff stage with a 4-0 aggregate score .
Australia_national_football_team	Having won the Oceania playoff , Australia now had to win a 2-leg playoff against Canada , the CONCACAF runner up .
Australia_national_football_team	The first leg was played in Canada on 31 July 1993 , with the Canadians winning the 1st leg 2-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	In the second leg , which was played on 15 August 1993 in Sydney , Australia managed a 2-1 win which saw the game go into extra time after a 3-3 aggregate scoreline .
Australia_national_football_team	The game went into a penalty shootout which was won by Australia 4-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia then qualified for the 2-leg playoff against the South American group 1 runner up , Argentina .
Australia_national_football_team	The first leg was played in Sydney on 31 October 1993 .
Australia_national_football_team	The 1st leg ended with a 1-1 draw .
Australia_national_football_team	On 17 November 1993 , the second leg was played in Argentina , with Argentina winning 1-0 and denying Australia a place at the 1994 World Cup in the United States .
Australia_national_football_team	After the game Argentine legend Diego Maradona was so impressed with the Socceroos performance that he said to then captain Paul Wade `` Your tears of pain , will one day be tears of joy '' .
Australia_national_football_team	Just to qualify for the 1994 World Cup Australia would have had to beat Argentina , the runners-up from the 1990 World Cup , and ranked 9th in the world at that time .
Australia_national_football_team	In 1997 Australia failed to qualify for the World Cup finals despite being undefeated in the qualifying rounds .
Australia_national_football_team	After winning the OFC qualifying tournament , Australia had to play Iran over two legs in one week , with the winner progressing to the World Cup finals to be held in France .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia , under coach Terry Venables , tied the away leg 1-1 and looked like they were going to proceed to the finals in France , initially leading 2-0 in the home game in Melbourne , until Iran managed to score two late goals to tie the game and progress to the finals on the away goals rule .
Australia_national_football_team	This match has been named one of the most memorable matches by many of the retired Australian and Iranian football players .
Australia_national_football_team	At the time the crowd that packed the MCG was the highest ever for an association football match in Australia .
Australia_national_football_team	Second and third-string line-ups thrashed a number of tiny island nations in a competition that made a mockery of the Confederation , including a world-record 22-0 win against Tonga , then smashed that record with a 31-0 win over American Samoa only two days later .
Australia_national_football_team	Still missing Harry Kewell and Mark Viduka , Australia comfortably beat New Zealand , their only real threat in the Oceania confederation .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia then once again had to win a two leg playoff in November , in order to advance to the World Cup finals to be held in South Korea and Japan .
Australia_national_football_team	On this occasion the opposition was the 5th placed South American team , Uruguay .
Australia_national_football_team	In the preceding four months Uruguay 's preparation had been six World Cup qualifying matches , as follows : beat # 2 ranked Brazil 1:0 ; drew 1:1 with # 8 ranked Colombia ; drew 1:1 with # 2 ranked Argentina .
Australia_national_football_team	In contrast , Australia 's preparation had included no qualifying games since two matches in 4 days in June , against # 81 ranked New Zealand , although had played two friendly matches - a loss to Japan in August and a 1:1 draw with France in November .
Australia_national_football_team	In the first leg in Melbourne , Australia won 1-0 after Kevin Muscat scored from a penalty kick ; however , Australia 's qualification campaign ended unsuccessfully as they lost 3-0 in the away leg in Montevideo just five days later with the South Americans proving too strong .
Australia_national_football_team	The team 's previously poor record in World Cup competition was not reflected in their reasonable performances against strong European and South American sides .
Australia_national_football_team	In 1988 , Australia defeated Argentina 4-1 in the Bicentennial Gold Cup .
Australia_national_football_team	In 1997 , Australia drew with Brazil 0-0 in the group stage and then defeated Uruguay 1-0 in the semi-finals to reach the 1997 FIFA Confederations Cup Final .
Australia_national_football_team	Another highlight for Australian football was the 3-1 victory over England in a friendly in London in 2003 .
Australia_national_football_team	The team drew 2-2 with the Solomon Islands , which combined with other results put that team ahead of New Zealand in the standings and meaning that the Solomon Islands qualified for the final playoff rather than the expected New Zealand .
Australia_national_football_team	Coach Frank Farina stood down from the position by `` mutual consent '' on 29 June 2005 after Australia failed to win a game at the 2005 Confederations Cup , citing ever increasing speculation over his position .
Australia_national_football_team	On 22 July , Guus Hiddink was announced by FIFA as the new national coach .
Australia_national_football_team	This announcement came after intense speculation by the Australian media over potential candidates and even a premature announcement from Hiddink himself .
Australia_national_football_team	After some initial training sessions with the Australian team in the Netherlands , his first campaign as national coach resulted in a 11-1 aggregate win over the Solomon Islands in the OFC Qualifying Tournament Final .
Australia_national_football_team	The remaining task for Hiddink and Australia was the Oceania-South America playoff against the fifth placed team from the CONMEBOL Qualifying Tournament for a place in the World Cup .
Australia_national_football_team	In October 2005 , Australia beat Jamaica 5-0 in a friendly in London .
Australia_national_football_team	The win was the Socceroos ' biggest win against a team ranked higher than them in the FIFA World Rankings list and also Australia 's biggest win against a country which has participated in the World Cup .
Australia_national_football_team	Again , there was a huge contrast in preparation .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia had only two recent qualifying matches , against # 138 Solomon Islands , only three days apart .
Australia_national_football_team	Uruguay 's preparation had included four qualifying matches , in the previous two months , including : beaten # 26 Colombia , drawn with # 33 Ecuador , and beaten # 4 Argentina .
Australia_national_football_team	Uruguay called for the first leg to be moved a day earlier , to 11 November .
Australia_national_football_team	This idea was rejected by Australia .
Australia_national_football_team	As a result , Uruguay had announced that they had moved the kick off time back five hours to 9:00 pm local time on 12 November .
Australia_national_football_team	This meant that Australia would miss their direct flight back to Sydney for the second leg .
Australia_national_football_team	This would also mean that Uruguay would have an extra day of preparation for the second leg .
Australia_national_football_team	However , this plan backfired on the Uruguayans .
Australia_national_football_team	Their plans to charter a plane for a direct flight to Sydney fell through ( they ended up flying over in economy class seating on a regular commercial flight ) .
Australia_national_football_team	When Uruguay asked to move the kickoff back , Australia , which by that time had arranged , with their sponsor Qantas , a specially fitted out 767 ( which included massage tables , and much room and space ) for immediately after the game , refused .
Australia_national_football_team	Eventually , FIFA stepped in and ordered the kickoff moved back to 6:00 pm local time .
Australia_national_football_team	Uruguay defeated Australia 1-0 in Montevideo on 12 November 2005 , after a header from Dario Rodriguez .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia had the better of their Uruguayan opponents for a lot of the match , but they could not capitalize on their opportunities .
Australia_national_football_team	In Sydney , on 16 November for the second leg of the qualifying series and in front of 82,698 fans at Telstra Stadium , Australia led Uruguay 1-0 after 90 minutes following a goal by Mark Bresciano in the first half .
Australia_national_football_team	The aggregate was tied , and extra time was played .
Australia_national_football_team	Neither team scored after two periods of extra time , bringing the game to a penalty shootout .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia won the penalty shootout 4-2 , making Australia the only team to ever qualify for a World Cup via a penalty shootout .
Australia_national_football_team	Australian goalkeeper Mark Schwarzer made two saves and John Aloisi scored the winning penalty .
Australia_national_football_team	Their ranking on the FIFA World Rankings improved in subsequent months , leapfrogging other qualified countries .
Australia_national_football_team	Many commentators and fans felt that the only way for Australia to progress was to abandon the Oceania Football Confederation .
Australia_national_football_team	Football had developed over time to place increasing importance on tournaments rather than friendly matches .
Australia_national_football_team	This established the Continental championships and their qualifiers as the major source of competitive matches for national teams .
Australia_national_football_team	This served to starve Australia of potential opponents and resulted in long gaps between fixtures for the national team .
Australia_national_football_team	Football broadcaster and former Socceroos captain Johnny Warren , expressed his desire for Australia to join Asia .
Australia_national_football_team	Despite previous attempts to do so , each notoriously ending in failure , a story was leaked from Tokyo in March 2005 suggesting that FIFA had entered into secret discussions with the AFC on this very issue .
Australia_national_football_team	On 23 March , the AFC Executive Committee made a unanimous decision to invite Australia to join the AFC .
Australia_national_football_team	AFC President , Mohammed Bin Hammam , outlined reasons for this decision .
Australia_national_football_team	As well as being a developed football nation , Australia brings a developed economy and this is actually what we want in football .
Australia_national_football_team	Besides Japan , Korea , China and Saudi Arabia if Australia joins the benefits are huge , this is what we 're after .
Australia_national_football_team	On 17 April , the OFC executive committee unanimously endorsed Australia 's proposed move .
Australia_national_football_team	Earlier , on 1 December , the AFC Executive Committee announced that Australia would be put into the ASEAN zone .
Australia_national_football_team	Currently , Australia is an invitee member of ASEAN Football Federation .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia was duly entered into the 2007 AFC Asian Cup qualification .
Australia_national_football_team	On 4 January , Australia was drawn into group D , alongside Bahrain , Lebanon and Kuwait .
Australia_national_football_team	Lebanon later withdrew due to recent military conflict in the area .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's first game as a member of the AFC was on 22 February , a 3-1 win away to Bahrain in the 2007 AFC Asian Cup qualification .
Australia_national_football_team	They subsequently qualified for the finals on 16 August after defeating Kuwait 2-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	In late December 2005 , Coach Guus Hiddink appointed former Dutch player , Johan Neeskens , as Assistant Coach , to work alongside Graham Arnold , Ron Smith , Tony Franken and Anthony Crea .
Australia_national_football_team	The home strip , similar to the 1974 outfit , is an entirely yellow shirt with green shorts .
Australia_national_football_team	The away strip is entirely obsidian blue with yellow trimmings ( the heraldic colors of Australia ) .
Australia_national_football_team	The jerseys were launched at a lavish ceremony at the Berlin Olympic Stadium in Berlin .
Australia_national_football_team	While the team was preparing for the World Cup , Socceroos player Tony Vidmar was ruled out after being diagnosed with a heart condition .
Australia_national_football_team	In all , the squad that won the qualification matches saw 5 changes in the lead-up the World Cup finals .
Australia_national_football_team	Joel Griffiths , Ahmad Elrich , Ljubo Milicevic , Tony Vidmar and Michael Thwaite were replaced by Joshua Kennedy , Mile Sterjovski , Michael Beauchamp , Craig Moore and Mark Milligan respectively .
Australia_national_football_team	As part of a national support effort for the Socceroos in Australia , the television network SBS ran a competition , `` Song for the Socceroos '' , in order to select a World Cup anthem for the Socceroos .
Australia_national_football_team	The winning song `` Green and Gold '' was announced on 16 May .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia won 1-0 thanks to a Josip Skoko volley early on in the match .
Australia_national_football_team	The match , at the 100,000 capacity Melbourne Cricket Ground , was sold out in only 2 hours , and was a great sendoff for Australia from home soil , despite the questionable quality of the Greek performance .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia played the Netherlands in a friendly match in Rotterdam on 4 June .
Australia_national_football_team	The Dutch , ranked # 3 in the world , went ahead in the 9th minute after goalkeeper Mark Schwarzer parried a Ruud van Nistelrooy shot , the Socceroos failed to clear the ball and van Nistelrooy scored with a follow-up strike .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's Tim Cahill equalised in the 53rd minute following a goal-line scramble after Mark Viduka hit the crossbar from a penalty kick .
Australia_national_football_team	The match ended in a 1-1 draw .
Australia_national_football_team	The only blemish was the dismissal of defender Luke Wilkshire in the 61st minute , after a wild challenge on Giovanni van Bronckhorst .
Australia_national_football_team	The next day , the Socceroos left for Germany .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia played a final pre-World Cup friendly against 123rd-ranked Liechtenstein on 7 June .
Australia_national_football_team	Defender Lucas Neill headed an own goal in the 8th minute , giving Liechtenstein the lead until Mile Sterjovski equalised in the 20th .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia struggled to gain a lead on their opponents until the final 15 minutes when a goal each from Joshua Kennedy and John Aloisi won Australia the game 3-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	Just days before Australia 's first World Cup match against Japan , it was reported in the west that the Japan Football Association chairman claimed the Socceroos were `` guilty of a lot of dirty fouls '' and that `` they target ankles in particular . ''
Australia_national_football_team	However , a further scrutiny of the original Japanese script reveals that there was a misinterpretation by the western media , possibly to spice up the competition .
Australia_national_football_team	While it is unclear who started this mistranslation , deliberately or otherwise , Saburo Kawabuchi of Japan Football Association later commented that this would not be the first or the last time mistranslation happens and should not be taken too seriously .
Australia_national_football_team	On 12 June , the Socceroos defeated Japan 3-1 in their opening game in Kaiserslautern , with Tim Cahill scoring two goals ( 84 ' , 89 ' ) and John Aloisi scoring one ( 92 + ' ) in the last eight minutes to claim their first World Cup finals victory .
Australia_national_football_team	An early controversial call by Egyptian referee Essam Abd El Fatah , that awarded a goal ( 26 ' ) to Shunsuke Nakamura , despite an apparent foul to Australian goalkeeper Mark Schwarzer , had the Australians playing catch-up until the last eight minutes .
Australia_national_football_team	Schwarzer and Viduka claimed that Abd El Fatah apologised over allowing Nakamura 's goal to stand after the incident , admitting he had made a mistake , although Abd El Fatah later denied making an apology and said that `` FIFA 's refereeing committee ... agreed unanimously that Japan 's goal against Australia was correct . ''
Australia_national_football_team	Both Cahill and Aloisi came in as substitutes in the second half of the game .
Australia_national_football_team	Also , no other team has scored three goals in the last seven minutes of a match in World Cup finals history .
Australia_national_football_team	On 18 June , hours before Australia 's second game against world champions Brazil , a British newspaper claimed that several Australian players had placed bets amongst themselves , which was said to be against FIFA regulations .
Australia_national_football_team	Tim Cahill admitted that teammates Lucas Neill and Archie Thompson bet that Cahill would score the first ever Australian goal at the World Cup .
Australia_national_football_team	Mark Viduka also said that the players were taking bets on who was going to be the first to score , and that goalkeeper Zeljko Kalac was the bookmaker .
Australia_national_football_team	FIFA have since cleared all players of any wrongdoing , by interpreting their regulations as referring to betting with professional bookmakers , rather than betting within a team .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia met Brazil in their second Group F game in Munich on 18 June .
Australia_national_football_team	The Australians held Brazil to a 0-0 half time scoreline before Adriano put Brazil in front ( 49 ' ) .
Australia_national_football_team	Brazil substitute Fred scored ( 90 ' ) with the help of substitute Robinho to give Brazil a 2-0 win , which saw the Brazilians go through to the second round .
Australia_national_football_team	A day later , following the Brazil game , Harry Kewell was in hot water after an altercation with the referee from the Brazil game .
Australia_national_football_team	FIFA announced that it would investigate the incident .
Australia_national_football_team	On 20 June , charges were dismissed against Kewell due to `` inconsistent reporting by match officials '' , allowing him to play the next game against Croatia .
Australia_national_football_team	On 22 June , Australia faced Croatia in Stuttgart .
Australia_national_football_team	The final score was 2-2 .
Australia_national_football_team	A goal from Darijo Srna in the second minute put Australia on the back foot .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia equalised with a penalty goal from Craig Moore ( 38 ' ) after Croatian defender Stjepan Tomas handballed near the Croatian goal .
Australia_national_football_team	Niko Kovac gave Croatia a 2-1 lead after halftime before Australia equalised again through Harry Kewell ( 79 ' ) in a moment described by SBS broadcast commentator Simon Hill as `` well , it just had to be Harry '' .
Australia_national_football_team	Kewell appeared to be offside for the goal , in a match riddled with errors .
Australia_national_football_team	The referee Graham Poll dismissed calls for a penalty in the 5th minute when Croatia 's Josip Šimunić appeared to wrestle striker Mark Viduka to the ground near goal .
Australia_national_football_team	Despite penalising Croatia for Stjepan Tomas ' handball in the 39th minute , he failed to penalize Tomas for exactly the same deed in the 75th minute , when Australia were trying to equalise again .
Australia_national_football_team	Towards the end of the match , Poll blew the final whistle at the moment that John Aloisi scored what would have been a winning goal , and then blew the final whistle again , before presenting Simunic with three yellow cards and then sending him off after the final whistle .
Australia_national_football_team	Here , Simunic is the world record holder for `` Most Yellow Cards in a Football Match . ''
Australia_national_football_team	Poll issued eight yellow cards resulting in three expulsions .
Australia_national_football_team	Brett Emerton was sent off for his second bookable offence ( although he was already suspended for the next match for receiving his second yellow card of the group stage earlier in the match ) .
Australia_national_football_team	The Daily Telegraph reported on 25 June that Graham Poll was dismissed from World Cup refereeing duties by FIFA , who claimed that his mistake was `` unacceptable '' .
Australia_national_football_team	As Brazil beat Japan 4-1 , Australia proceeded to the next round to face Italy .
Australia_national_football_team	On 26 June , Australia met Italy in Kaiserslautern .
Australia_national_football_team	Kewell was unavailable for the game , entering the stadium on crutches reportedly suffering from an attack of gout and infected blisters ( later diagnosed as septic arthritis ) .
Australia_national_football_team	The score at half-time was 0-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	Italy went down to 10 men due to the red card ( 51 ' ) given to Marco Materazzi for a two-footed tackle on Mark Bresciano .
Australia_national_football_team	Otherwise , six yellow cards were issued in total .
Australia_national_football_team	Almost three minutes into stoppage time , with the score still at 0-0 and Australia being pushed into their own half , a controversial penalty was awarded to Italy when Fabio Grosso fell under a Lucas Neill challenge in the final seconds of the match .
Australia_national_football_team	Francesco Totti scored from the spot ( 95 ' ) and the game ended immediately with Australia eliminated .
Australia_national_football_team	Coach Guus Hiddink officially ended his reign as the coach of the Socceroos following the 1-0 loss to Italy and took the managerial job with Russia .
Australia_national_football_team	Australian assistant coach Graham Arnold branded the penalty a `` joke '' , to the agreement of several Australian players , including Tim Cahill , who believed Grosso should have been cautioned for diving .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia , led by Graham Arnold , went to their first Asian Cup sending a strong squad which included 15 players from the World Cup team .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia was drawn in Group A alongside ( co-host ) Thailand , Oman and Iraq .
Australia_national_football_team	In their first match , Australia were only able to earn a 1-1 draw against a lower-ranked Oman team .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia played poorly , with Oman leading for most of the match after Badar Al-Maimani scored in the 32nd minute , but were once again saved by Tim Cahill who scored a late equaliser in the 92nd minute after coming on as a substitute in the second half .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia lost their second group match 3-1 to eventual Asian Cup winners Iraq , with Lucas Neill receiving a red card ( 90 ' ) , following two yellow cards .
Australia_national_football_team	Mark Viduka scored the lone goal for the Australians in the 47th minute of the match which at that point in the game was the equaliser but Iraq scored another two goals to win .
Australia_national_football_team	In the third match of the group stage , Australia defeated Thailand 4-0 with Mark Viduka scoring two goals , with Michael Beauchamp and Harry Kewell scoring one goal each .
Australia_national_football_team	The victory assured Australia 's progression to the quarter final stage of the tournament .
Australia_national_football_team	After drawing 1-1 with Japan after extra time , Australia exited the tournament on penalties at the quarter final stage .
Australia_national_football_team	The first two Australian penalty kicks were both unsuccessful by Harry Kewell and Lucas Neill with Australia eventually bowing out 4-3 to end their inaugural participation in Asia 's most prestigious football tournament .
Australia_national_football_team	In a friendly international at the MCG on 11 September 2007 , the Socceroos were defeated by Argentina one goal to nil .
Australia_national_football_team	The friendly was Graham Arnold 's last game as head coach .
Australia_national_football_team	It had been widely speculated that Dutchman Dick Advocaat would take over as Head Coach for the Socceroos 2010 World Cup Qualifiers by the end of 2007 but he backed out of a contract with the FFA to continue coaching Zenit Petersburg .
Australia_national_football_team	It has been reported that FFA is considering legal action against both person and club .
Australia_national_football_team	As a result the Socceroo 's head coach position was left open , with technical director Rob Baan the caretaker for a match against Nigeria at Loftus Road , London ( Australia winning 1-0 . )
Australia_national_football_team	The position was filled on 6 December 2007 when the FFA announced Pim Verbeek as the new head coach .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos were seeded to enter the AFC qualification campaign in the third round alongside Iran , Saudi Arabia , South Korea and Japan .
Australia_national_football_team	They were drawn into a group composed of Qatar , Iraq and China with the media dubbing it the `` group of death '' .
Australia_national_football_team	Fixtures started in February 2008 , with a home match against Qatar at the Telstra Dome in Melbourne giving Australia a 3-0 victory .
Australia_national_football_team	This was Pim Verbeek 's first competitive match in charge of the Socceroos .
Australia_national_football_team	The majority of the Australian squad consisted of overseas , mainly European based , players after Pim Verbeek announced the local A-league was not yet up to World Cup standards .
Australia_national_football_team	A week after the match , Australia moved up to 38th on the FIFA World Rankings .
Australia_national_football_team	In the second group game , Australia drew 0-0 with China with Mark Schwarzer saving a penalty in the last few minutes .
Australia_national_football_team	In their 3rd out of 6 qualifiers on Sunday , 1 June , Australia beat Iraq at Suncorp Stadium , Brisbane , 1-0 , with a headed goal from Harry Kewell proving the difference between the two teams early in the 2nd half of play .
Australia_national_football_team	In the return match in Dubai , Iraq defeated Australia 1-0 through a wonder strike from Emad Mohammed .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia then defeated Qatar 3-1 on 14 June in Doha to progress to the fourth round of the AFC qualifiers .
Australia_national_football_team	Their final game in 3rd round qualifying ended in a 1-0 home defeat to China .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia was drawn alongside Japan , Bahrain , Qatar and Uzbekistan in the fourth round of Asian World Cup qualification , which commenced with a 1-0 victory over the Uzbeks in Tashkent on 10 September 2008 .
Australia_national_football_team	Scott Chipperfield 's run was unmarked and he comfortably headed in a Luke Wilkshire cross .
Australia_national_football_team	They then proceeded to beat Qatar 4-0 at Suncorp Stadium , Brisbane , to go top of the group , with goals scored by Tim Cahill and Josh Kennedy with Brett Emerton scoring a brace for the home side .
Australia_national_football_team	The game was delayed 30min ( and close to abandoned ) after a torrential rainstorm hit Brisbane Stadium prior to the match .
Australia_national_football_team	Their next match was against Bahrain on 19 November .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia managed a 1-0 victory despite a brilliant performance by the Bahrainis and a disappointing performance by Australia .
Australia_national_football_team	Both the Australian coach and players admitted they were lucky to take the points which came courtesy of a Marco Bresciano goal in the 93rd minute .
Australia_national_football_team	They dedicated the win to Craig Moore who missed the match following surgery for testicular cancer .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia remained top of the group with 10 points after 4 games following a 0-0 draw away against Japan .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos were on the brink of qualifying after a convincing 2-0 win over Uzbekistan on 1 April in Sydney .
Australia_national_football_team	After a lacklustre first half , the Socceroos scored two goals with a Josh Kennedy header in the 66th minute and a Harry Kewell penalty in the 73rd minute after Richard Garcia was taken down in the penalty box .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia then secured their place in South Africa after holding Qatar 0-0 at Doha on 5 June .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's qualification was already assured before the final two games , both home fixtures .
Australia_national_football_team	In Sydney on Wednesday 10 June , goals to Mile Sterjovski and David Carney gave Australia a 2-0 victory over Bahrain .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's final qualification game ended with a 2-1 victory over Japan , Australia coming back from a goal in the 40th minute by Japan 's Marcus Tulio Tanaka with Tim Cahill 's equalising header in the 59th minute , and his winning goal 17 minutes later off a Nicky Carle corner .
Australia_national_football_team	This victory left Australia top of Group A ahead of Japan by 5 clear points .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia were drawn into Group D of the 2010 FIFA World Cup , featuring three-time world champion Germany , Ghana and Serbia .
Australia_national_football_team	Prior to leaving for South Africa , Australia played a warm-up game in Melbourne against New Zealand .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia played poorly with Vince Grella and Tim Cahill both performing dangerous tackles on Leo Bertos which could have earned red cards in competitive fixtures .
Australia_national_football_team	Despite trailing 1-0 at half-time , Australia managed to equalize through Dario Vidosic in the second half , with Brett Holman scoring the winner in injury time for a 2-1 victory .
Australia_national_football_team	In South Africa , Australia played another warm up game against Denmark in Johannesburg and won 1-0 , a single goal from towering striker Joshua Kennedy proving to be decisive .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's final warm up game before beginning their World Cup campaign was against United States with Australia suffering a 3-1 defeat and Tim Cahill scoring the only goal .
Australia_national_football_team	On 14 June 2010 , Australia faced Germany in Durban .
Australia_national_football_team	Pim Verbeek surprisingly chose to play without a recognized striker .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia were comprehensively defeated 4-0 , with goals by Podolski and Klose in the first half , followed by two more goals in the second half after Australia was reduced to ten men , due to Tim Cahill being sent off with a straight red card for a tackle from behind on Bastian Schweinsteiger .
Australia_national_football_team	Pim Verbeek was heavily criticised for his tactics , with chief SBS Football Analyst Craig Foster calling for his immediate sacking .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia 's second group match against Ghana resulted in a draw of 1-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia shot its only goal early in the first half by Brett Holman after Ghana 's goalkeeper Richard Kingson fumbled the ball following a Mark Bresciano freekick .
Australia_national_football_team	Shortly after , a goal-bound strike from Ghana 's Jonathan Mensah was blocked on the goal line by Harry Kewell 's upper arm , resulting in a penalty kick and a straight red card for Kewell .
Australia_national_football_team	Ghanaian striker Asamoah Gyan scored the equalizing goal .
Australia_national_football_team	Despite the man advantage , Ghana were mostly limited to long-range shots on Australia 's goal , and some desperate defending from Australia saw the game finish a draw .
Australia_national_football_team	In their final group match against Serbia , Tim Cahill was back from suspension and scored via a header in the second half to allow Australia to go 1-0 up .
Australia_national_football_team	Only four minutes later , Brett Holman doubled the scoreline to 2-0 with an impressive long-range effort .
Australia_national_football_team	Late in the second half , Serbia managed to score a late goal through Marko Pantelić after Australian goalkeeper Mark Schwarzer fumbled the ball , and the game ended 2-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	Germany had defeated Ghana 1-0 , which meant that both Australia and Ghana finished on 4 points , but Ghana progressed to the knockout stage due to their superior goal difference .
Australia_national_football_team	Pim Verbeek completed his term as Australian coach at the end of the 2010 World Cup .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos were drawn in Group B for the 2011 AFC Asian Cup qualifying stage along with Oman , Kuwait and Indonesia .
Australia_national_football_team	The top two teams from the group progressed to the finals in Qatar .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia progressed through to the 2011 finals in Qatar , topping Group B with 11 points with Kuwait coming in second with 8 points .
Australia_national_football_team	After qualifying for the 2011 AFC Asian Cup , Australia were drawn against Bahrain , India and South Korea in Group C. After defeating India 4-0 and drawing 1-1 with South Korea , the Socceroos went into the match against Bahrain needing only a point to progress .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos won 1-0 and topped their group .
Australia_national_football_team	On 23 January , Australia edged Iraq , 1-0 , in the quarterfinal .
Australia_national_football_team	The match went into extra time with Harry Kewell heading in a goal in the 117th minute just inside the 18-yard box .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia went on to destroy Uzbekistan , 6-0 , in the semifinals to set up a final against Japan on 29 January , which they lost in extra time 1-0 , becoming runners-up .
Australia_national_football_team	After a number of promising games under new manager , Holger Osieck , including a highly successful 2011 Asian Cup campaign , preparations got underway for the 2014 FIFA World Cup qualification ( AFC ) .
Australia_national_football_team	The Asian qualifiers began in September and prior to these crucial encounters , FFA organised a number of friendlies against the All Whites , Serbia , Wales and Malaysia .
Australia_national_football_team	In March 2011 , the Socceroos scheduled a game against world footballing powerhouse , Germany in Mönchengladbach , and came out victorious defeating them 2-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	On 5 June Australia defeated New Zealand 3-0 in Adelaide .
Australia_national_football_team	Two days later they drew 0-0 with Serbia in Melbourne .
Australia_national_football_team	On 31 July , Australia got drawn in Group D along with Saudi Arabia , Oman and Thailand .
Australia_national_football_team	On 10 August , Australia played Wales in a friendly match in Cardiff , with Australia coming away victorious 2-1 .
Australia_national_football_team	Tim Cahill and Robbie Kruse scored the goals for Australia .
Australia_national_football_team	The Group stages started on 2 September .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos did n't start well in their first game at Suncorp Stadium , Brisbane against Thailand and were lucky to eek out the three points after going down 1-0 courtesy of a Teerasil Dangda goal for Thailand .
Australia_national_football_team	Josh Kennedy and Alex Brousque canceled out Teerasil 's strike to give Australia a 2-1 win .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos then traveled to Saudi Arabia the match was expected to be Australia 's toughest match in the group but the Socceroos put in a good performance and ran out 3-1 winners with Josh Kennedy netting twice and Luke Wilkshire converting from the penalty spot .
Australia_national_football_team	Before the third qualifying match , Australia played Asian minnows Malaysia in Canberra .
Australia_national_football_team	Given they were in the middle of an Asian qualifying tournament , coach Holger Osieck felt it was better for his team to play against an Asian opponent , instead of a European of South American team .
Australia_national_football_team	He felt they would get more benefit playing a quick tempo Asian style , as opposed to a stronger , more physical European style .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia won the match 5-0 .
Australia_national_football_team	Luke Wilkshire scored an early goal , before a double each to Josh Kennedy and Alex Brosque sealed a comfortable win .
Australia_national_football_team	While the match had its detractors , the hit-out proved necessary .
Australia_national_football_team	The next match against Oman was to be played in Sydney .
Australia_national_football_team	Josh Kennedy continued his fantastic goal scoring form with one goal , Mile Jedinak and Brett Holman contributed goals as the Socceroos ran out 3-0 victors .
Australia_national_football_team	The Socceroos then had to go to Muscat , Oman to play their 4th match in Group D. Many thought that Australia would ease past Oman due to Oman 's poor performance in the game in Sydney but Oman stunned Australia winning 1-0 in a tightly contested match in which Australia were disallowed a goal which many thought should have counted .
Australia_national_football_team	The Australian team then proceeded to defeat Thailand 1-0 at home which ensured that they will top the group and thus qualify for the next round of qualifying with 1 game to spare in the third round .
Australia_national_football_team	In their last game of the third round of 2014 Asian World Cup Qualification the Socceroos hosted Saudi Arabia at AAMI Park in Melbourne .
Australia_national_football_team	It was a dead rubber with the Socceroos already qualified for the fourth round so Holger Oseick fielded a number of returning fringe players such as : James Troisi , Mark Milligan , Jade North and Mark Bresciano .
Australia_national_football_team	The Saudis took the lead through Al Dawsari and were dominating when the Socceroos equalised through Alex Brosque but the Saudis took the lead into half time when Al Shamrani scored to give the Saudis a 2-1 lead .
Australia_national_football_team	Then the Socceroos came out stronger in the second half and a 3 goals in 3 minutes from Alex Brosque , Harry Kewell and Brett Emerton gave the Socceroos a 4-2 lead which they held to finish the game victors by 2 goals .
Australia_national_football_team	The AFC Asian Cup in 2015 will take place in Australia .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia have already qualified as hosts and runner-up of the 2011 series .
Australia_national_football_team	North Korea , Japan and South Korea have also qualified .
Australia_national_football_team	Australia joined AFC in 2006 .

Andrew_Huxley	Sir Andrew Fielding Huxley , OM , FRS ( 22 November 1917 - 30 May 2012 ) was a Nobel Prize-winning English physiologist and biophysicist .
Andrew_Huxley	Huxley was born in Hampstead , London , England on November 22 , 1917 , he was the youngest son of the writer and editor Leonard Huxley by his second wife Rosalind Bruce , and hence half-brother of the writer Aldous Huxley and fellow biologist Julian Huxley , and grandson of the biologist T. H. Huxley .
Andrew_Huxley	He was educated at Westminster School in Central London , where he was a King 's Scholar , before going to study Natural Sciences at Trinity College , Cambridge .
Andrew_Huxley	In 1947 he married Jocelyn Richenda Gammell ( Chenda ) Pease ( 1925-2003 ) , the daughter of the geneticist Michael Pease and his wife Helen Bowen Wedgwood , a daughter of the first Lord Wedgwood , and is thus affiliated with the Darwin-Wedgwood family .
Andrew_Huxley	Lady Huxley had notable connections to scientific dynasties and Fabian socialism .
Andrew_Huxley	She was sister of Rendel Sebastian `` Bas '' Pease , and a niece of the anthropological Camilla Wedgwood , as well as daughter of a geneticist .
Andrew_Huxley	They have one son and five daughters : Janet Rachel Huxley ( born 20 April 1948 ) Stewart Leonard Huxley ( born 19 December 1949 ) Camilla Rosalind Huxley ( born 12 March 1952 ) Eleanor Bruce Huxley ( born 21 February 1959 ) Henrietta Catherine Huxley ( born 25 December 1960 ) Clare Marjory Pease Huxley ( born 4 November 1962 ) He won the 1963 Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine for his experimental and mathematical work with Alan Hodgkin on the basis of nerve action potentials , the electrical impulses that enable the activity of an organism to be coordinated by a central nervous system .
Andrew_Huxley	Hodgkin and Huxley shared the prize that year with John Eccles , who was cited for research on synapses .
Andrew_Huxley	Hodgkin and Huxley 's findings led the pair to hypothesize the existence of ion channels , which were isolated only decades later .
Andrew_Huxley	Together with the Swiss physiologist Robert Stämpfli he evidenced the existence of saltatory conduction in myelinated nerve fibers .
Andrew_Huxley	Huxley was elected a Fellow of the Royal Society on 17 March 1955 .
Andrew_Huxley	He was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II on 12 November 1974 .
Andrew_Huxley	Sir Andrew was then appointed to the Order of Merit on 11 November 1983 .
Andrew_Huxley	The experimental measurements on which the pair based their action potential theory represent one of the earliest applications of a technique of electrophysiology known as the voltage clamp .
Andrew_Huxley	The second critical element of their research used the giant axon of the Atlantic squid ( Loligo pealei ) , which enabled them to record ionic currents as they would not have been able to do in almost any other neuron , such cells being too small to study by the techniques of the time .
Andrew_Huxley	The experiments started at the University of Cambridge , beginning in 1935 with frog sciatic nerve , and soon after they continued their work using squid giant axons at the Marine Biological Association Laboratory in Plymouth .
Andrew_Huxley	In 1939 , reporting work done in Plymouth , Alan Hodgkin and Andrew Huxley published a short paper in the journal Nature announcing their achievement of recording action potentials from inside a nerve fiber .
Andrew_Huxley	Research was interrupted by World War II but after resuming their experimental work in Plymouth , the pair published their theory in 1952 .
Andrew_Huxley	In the paper , they describe one of the earliest computational models in biochemistry , that is the basis of most of the models used in Neurobiology during the following four decades .
Andrew_Huxley	He continued to hold college and university posts in Cambridge until 1960 , when he became head of the Department of Physiology at University College London .
Andrew_Huxley	For his research , in 1963 he was awarded the Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine .
Andrew_Huxley	In 1969 he was appointed to a Royal Society Research Professorship which he holds in the Department of Physiology at University College London .
Andrew_Huxley	He maintained up to his death his position as a fellow at Trinity College , Cambridge , teaching in physiology , natural sciences and medicine .
Andrew_Huxley	He was also a fellow of Imperial College London in 1980 .
Andrew_Huxley	From his experimental work with Hodgkin , Huxley developed a set of differential equations that provided a mathematical explanation for nerve impulses-the `` action potential '' .
Andrew_Huxley	This work provided the foundation for the all of the current work on voltage-sensitive membrane channels , which are responsible for the functioning of animal nervous systems .
Andrew_Huxley	Quite separately , he developed the mathematical equations for the operation of myosin `` cross-bridges '' that generate the sliding forces between actin and myosin filaments , which cause the contraction of skeletal muscles .
Andrew_Huxley	These equations presented an entirely new paradigm for understanding muscle contraction , which has been extended to provide our understanding of almost all of the movements produced by cells above the level of bacteria .
Andrew_Huxley	Huxley died in 2012 in his home of Grantchester , Cambridgeshire , England from unknown causes .
Andrew_Huxley	He was survived by his six children , grandchildren , and great-grandchildren .
Andrew_Huxley	His wife Richenda , Lady Huxley died in 2003 .
Andrew_Huxley	A memorial service was held in Trinity College , Cambridge , and the physiologist was buried on the grounds of the college 's campus .
Alphonse_Mucha	Alfons Maria Mucha ( Czech pronunciation : ( ˈalfons ˈmuxa ) ( listen ) ; 24 July 1860 - 14 July 1939 ) , known in English as Alphonse Mucha , was a Czech Art Nouveau painter and decorative artist , known best for his distinct style .
Alphonse_Mucha	He produced many paintings , illustrations , advertisements , postcards , and designs .
Alphonse_Mucha	Alphonse Maria Mucha was born in the town of Ivančice , Moravia ( the present Czech Republic ) .
Alphonse_Mucha	Although his singing abilities allowed him to continue his education through high school in the Moravian capital of Brno , drawing had been his main hobby since childhood .
Alphonse_Mucha	He worked at decorative painting jobs in Moravia , mostly painting theatrical scenery .
Alphonse_Mucha	In 1879 , he relocated to Vienna to work for a major Viennese theatrical design company , while informally augmenting his artistic education .
Alphonse_Mucha	When a fire destroyed his employer 's business during 1881 he returned to Moravia , to do freelance decorative and portrait painting .
Alphonse_Mucha	Count Karl Khuen of Mikulov hired Mucha to decorate Hrušovany Emmahof Castle with murals , and was impressed enough that he agreed to sponsor Mucha 's formal training at the Munich Academy of Fine Arts .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha moved to Paris in 1887 , and continued his studies at Académie Julian and Académie Colarossi .
Alphonse_Mucha	In addition to his studies , he worked at producing magazine and advertising illustrations .
Alphonse_Mucha	About Christmas 1894 , Mucha happened to go into a print shop where there was a sudden and unexpected need for a new advertising poster for a play featuring Sarah Bernhardt , the most famous actress in Paris , at the Théâtre de la Renaissance on the Boulevard Saint-Martin .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha volunteered to produce a lithographed poster within two weeks , and on 1 January 1895 , the advertisement for the play Gismonda by Victorien Sardou was posted in the city , where it attracted much attention .
Alphonse_Mucha	Bernhardt was so satisfied with the success of this first poster that she began a six-year contract with Mucha .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha produced a flurry of paintings , posters , advertisements , and book illustrations , as well as designs for jewelry , carpets , wallpaper , and theater sets in what was termed initially the Mucha Style but became known as Art Nouveau ( French for ` new art ' ) .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha 's works frequently featured beautiful young women in flowing , vaguely Neoclassical-looking robes , often surrounded by lush flowers which sometimes formed halos behind their heads .
Alphonse_Mucha	In contrast with contemporary poster makers he used pale pastel colors .
Alphonse_Mucha	The 1900 Universal Exhibition in Paris spread the `` Mucha style '' internationally , of which Mucha said `` I think ( the Exposition Universelle ) made some contribution toward bringing aesthetic values into arts and crafts . ''
Alphonse_Mucha	He decorated the Bosnia and Herzegovina Pavilion and collaborated with decorating the Austrian Pavilion .
Alphonse_Mucha	His Art Nouveau style was often imitated .
Alphonse_Mucha	The Art Nouveau style however , was one that Mucha attempted to disassociate himself from throughout his life ; he always insisted that rather than maintaining any fashionable stylistic form , his paintings were entirely a product of himself and Czech art .
Alphonse_Mucha	He declared that art existed only to communicate a spiritual message , and nothing more ; hence his frustration at the fame he gained by his commercial art , when he most wanted to concentrate on more artistic projects .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha married Maruška ( Marie\/Maria ) Chytilová on 10 June 1906 , in Prague .
Alphonse_Mucha	The couple visited the U.S. from 1906 to 1910 , during which time their daughter , Jaroslava , was born in New York City .
Alphonse_Mucha	They also had a son , Jiří , ( born 12 March 1915 in Prague ; died 5 April 1991 in Prague ) who later became a well known journalist , writer , screenwriter , author of autobiographical novels and studies of the works of his father .
Alphonse_Mucha	In the U.S. , Alphonse expected to earn money to fund his nationalistic projects to demonstrate to Czechs that he had not `` sold out '' .
Alphonse_Mucha	He was assisted by millionaire Charles R. Crane , who used his fortune to help promote revolutions and , after meeting Thomas Masaryk , Slavic nationalism .
Alphonse_Mucha	Alphonse and his family returned to the Czech lands and settled in Prague , where he decorated the Theater of Fine Arts , contributed his time and talent to create the murals in the Mayor 's Office at the Municipal House , and other landmarks around the city .
Alphonse_Mucha	When Czechoslovakia won its independence after World War I , Mucha designed the new postage stamps , banknotes , and other government documents for the new state .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha considered his publication Le Pater to be his printed masterpiece , and referred to it in The Sun of 5 January 1900 as what he had `` put ( his ) soul into '' .
Alphonse_Mucha	Printed on 20 December 1899 , Le Pater was Mucha 's occult examination of the themes of The Lord 's Prayer and only 510 copies were produced .
Alphonse_Mucha	Mucha spent many years working on what he considered his life 's fine art masterpiece , The Slav Epic ( Slovanská epopej ) , a series of twenty huge paintings depicting the history of the Czech and the Slavic people in general , bestowed to the city of Prague in 1928 .
Alphonse_Mucha	He had wanted to complete a series such as this , a celebration of Slavic history , since he was young .
Alphonse_Mucha	Since 1963 the series has been on display in the chateau in Moravský Krumlov the South Moravian Region in the Czech Republic .
Alphonse_Mucha	The rising tide of fascism during the late 1930s resulted in Mucha 's works , as well as his Slavic nationalism , being denounced in the press as ` reactionary ' .
Alphonse_Mucha	When German troops moved into Czechoslovakia during the spring of 1939 , Mucha was among the first persons to be arrested by the Gestapo .
Alphonse_Mucha	During his interrogation , the aging artist became ill with pneumonia .
Alphonse_Mucha	Though released eventually , he may have been weakened by this event .
Alphonse_Mucha	He died in Prague on 14 July 1939 , due to lung infection , and was interred there in the Vyšehrad cemetery .
